Liability for Destruction of Borrowed Item without Transgression
States Hanafi non-liability and refutes opposing madhahib with proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on borrower liability for accidental destruction, explain the proofs, and compare it with the positions of al-Shafi'i, Ahmad, and Malik.

Core Idea
In Hanafi law, a borrower is not liable for accidental loss of a borrowed item unless transgression occurred.

This lesson examines a key inter-madhhab dispute regarding liability (daman) for a borrowed item (ariyah) that is destroyed without any transgression (ta'addi) by the borrower. The Hanafi school holds that the borrower is not liable, while the Shafi'i, Maliki, and Hanbali schools impose liability in certain circumstances. We will explore the textual proofs and rational arguments behind each position, and see how the Hanafi school interprets the hadith that seem to impose liability.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school holds that the borrower is not liable for accidental destruction of a borrowed item unless transgression (ta'addi) occurred. This is the default ruling from the zahir al-riwayah.
2
Identify the opponents and their views
Al-Shafi'i holds the borrower liable if the item perishes outside the state of use. Ahmad holds liability unless stipulated otherwise. Malik holds liability for items whose destruction is normally hidden (e.g., clothes, money).
These positions are based on the borrower's possession for benefit or ease of concealment.
3
Follow the opponents' proofs
Shafi'i argues that the borrower takes possession for his own benefit, making him a cause for liability. Ahmad and Malik rely on general principles of guarantee and practical considerations.
The hadith 'al-ariyatu amanatu mu'adatun' is cited by all sides.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafis reinterpret the hadith: 'mamdunah' means liability for return (daman al-radd), not for value. The story of Safwan is explained as a case of public necessity or a stipulation of liability, not a general rule. Rational proof: liability requires a preventing hand (yad dhamana), which only exists with transgression.
This response reconciles the hadith with the principle of non-liability.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: In Hanafi law, a borrower is not liable for accidental loss, whereas in other schools he may be liable depending on the item or circumstances. This affects everyday lending and borrowing in Islamic finance and community dealings.
Stipulating liability in the loan contract is a point of internal Hanafi disagreement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو هلكت بلا تعد لم يضمن، وقال الشافعي: يضمن إذا هلكت في غير حالة الاستعمال؛ لأنه قبض مال الغير لنفسه فكان سببا للضمان وبه قال أحمد لله، وعن أحمد مه: لو شرط الضمان يضمن وإلا لا، وقال مالك: ما يخفى هلاكه كالثياب والأثمان يضمن، وإلا لا، ولنا أن الضمان إنما يجب بإخراج العين من أن يكون منتفعاً بها في حق المالك بإثبات اليد المانعة، ولا يوجد هذا إلا عند التعدي. رمز الحقائق: ٢٥٦/٢] ولم يوجد فإن قلت: روى الترمذي أنه عليه قال: "العارية أمانة مؤداة مضمونة وروى البخاري وأبو داود أنه عليه استعار أدرعاً من الصفوان بن أمية يوم خيبر، فقال صفوان أغصبا يا محمد؟ فقال: "لا بل هو عارية مضمونة" قلت: الحديث الأول محمول على ضمان الرد والخلاف في ضمان الرد بالقيمة وكذا الحديث الثاني، وقيل: كان الأخذ في حديث صفوان بغير إذنه لحاجة المسلمين ولهذا قال: أغصباً يا محمد؟ وعند حاجة الناس يرخص تناول مال الغير بغير إذنه بشرط الضمان كحالة المخمصة ؛ ولأنه شرط له الضمان والعارية إذا شرط فيها الضمان يضمن عندنا في رواية، قلت: في "خلاصة الفتاوى" ناقلاً . عن "المنتقى": رجل قال لآخر: أعرني ثوبك فإن ضاع فأنا له ضامن قال: لا يضمن وفي "التحفة: إذا شرط الضمان في العارية هل يصح أم لا ؟ فالمشايخ يختلفون فيه. (عيني)
And if it perishes without transgression, he is not liable. Al-Shafi'i said: He is liable if it perishes outside the state of use because he took possession of another's property for his own benefit, so he became a cause for liability. Ahmad agreed with him. It is reported from Ahmad that if he stipulates liability, he is liable, otherwise not. Malik said: That whose destruction is hidden, like clothes and dirhams, is liable, otherwise not. Our evidence: Liability is only obligatory by removing the item from being benefited from in the right of the owner through establishing a preventing hand, and this occurs only with transgression. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 256/2) And it has not occurred. If you say: al-Tirmidhi narrated that he (peace be upon him) said: 'The loan is a trust, to be repaid, guaranteed.' And al-Bukhari and Abu Dawud narrated that he borrowed coats of mail from Safwan ibn Umayya on the day of Khaybar, and Safwan said, 'Is it plunder, O Muhammad?' He said, 'No, rather it is a loan, guaranteed.' I say: The first hadith is interpreted as liability for return, and the dispute is about liability for return with value, and so too the second hadith. And it is said: The taking in the hadith of Safwan was without his permission due to the need of the Muslims, therefore he said 'Is it plunder?'. And at times of need, consumption of another's property without permission is permitted on condition of liability, like in a famine. And because he stipulated liability for him, and the loan, if liability is stipulated in it, becomes liable according to us in one transmission. I say: In Khulasat al-Fatawa, quoting from al-Muntaqa: A man said to another, 'Lend me your garment, and if it is lost I am liable for it,' he said: He is not liable. And in al-Tuhfah: If liability is stipulated in the loan, is it valid or not? The mashayikh differ on it. (Ayni)
Source pages p. 122

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute. The Hanafi ruling is that the borrower is not liable for accidental destruction of the borrowed item without transgression (ta'addi). The commentary presents the positions of Shafi'i, Ahmad, and Malik, each imposing liability in certain cases: Shafi'i if the destruction occurs outside use, Ahmad if no stipulation, Malik if the item is easily hidden. The Hanafi proof is that liability only arises from a preventing hand (yad dhamana), which requires transgression. The two hadiths that seem to impose liability are addressed: 'The loan is a trust, to be repaid, guaranteed' is interpreted as liability for return (daman al-radd) not for value; the story of Safwan is explained as a special case of public necessity where the Prophet borrowed without permission but agreed to guarantee, or because he stipulated liability. The passage then discusses a transmission where stipulating liability makes the loan guaranteed, but this is not the relied-upon view. Later Hanafi scholars differ on the validity of stipulating liability in a loan. Thus, the default ruling is non-liability.

Key Terms
تعد (ta'addi): Transgression or misuse beyond the permitted use.
ضمان (daman): Liability to compensate for loss or damage.
عارية مضمونة (ariyah mamdunah): A loan that carries liability for the borrower; either by nature or by stipulation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling if a borrowed item is destroyed without any transgression by the borrower?
A) The borrower must pay the value.
B) The borrower is not liable.
C) The borrower is liable if the item is hidden.
D) The borrower is liable if the destruction occurred outside use.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a borrower is not liable for accidental loss or destruction of a borrowed item unless transgression or misuse occurred.

Borrower Cannot Rent or Pledge the Borrowed Item
Prohibition of renting and pledging borrowed items.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a borrower cannot rent or pledge a borrowed item and explain the reasoning.

Core Idea
A borrower cannot rent or pledge because that would impose binding obligations on a non-binding loan.

The borrowed item (ariyah) is a non-binding contract; the borrower has permission to use but not to transfer ownership. Renting or pledging would create binding obligations that conflict with the nature of the loan. This lesson examines why these actions are prohibited and the consequences if they occur.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prohibited actions
The text explicitly states that the borrower cannot rent (ijarah) or pledge (rahn) the borrowed item. Identify these two actions as the core prohibitions.
These are distinct from lending (i'arah) which is allowed under conditions.
2
Understand the reasoning for renting
The text explains that rental is a binding contract (lazim), while loan is non-binding (ghayr lazim). Allowing rental would either make the loan binding or the rental non-binding, both contradictions.
This is a logical argument based on the nature of the contracts.
3
Understand the reasoning for pledging
Pledging is using the item to secure a debt. The borrower does not own the item, so it is using another's property without permission, akin to a deposit (wadi'ah).
The text compares it to wadi'ah (deposit) where the same prohibition applies.
4
Analyze the liability if rented out and destroyed
If the borrower rents it out and it is destroyed, the lender can hold either the borrower or the lessee liable. The borrower is liable because he acted without permission (ta'addi); the lessee because he took possession without the owner's consent.
The owner chooses whom to sue; the recourse between them depends on knowledge.
5
Distinguish from depositing
The text notes that the borrower may deposit (wadi'ah) the item with another according to the mufta bihi view, unlike renting or pledging.
Depositing is not a transfer of ownership or binding contract.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا تؤجر أي ولا تؤجر العارية؛ لأن الإجارة أقوى؛ لأنها لازمة، فلو ملكها لزم لزوم ما لا يلزم، وهو العارية، أو عدم لزوم ما يلزم وهو الإجارة [البحر الرائق: ٤٠٦/٧] : ولا ترهن كالوديعة فإن آجر فعطبت ،ضمن ويعير ما لا يختلف بالمستعمل، فلو أي المستعير العارية المستعير المستعير قيدها بوقت أو منفعة أو بهما، لا يتجاوز عما سَمَّاه، أي المعير العارية كالشهر مثلا كركوب الدابة أي المستعير ولا ترهن لأن الرهن إيفاء وليس له أن يوفي دينه بمال غيره بغير إذنه، وله أن يودع على المفتى به، وهو المختار، وصحح بعضهم عدمه، ويتفرع عليه ما لو أرسلها على يد أجنبي، فهلكت يضمن على الثاني لا الأول، وسيأتي قريبا. [البحر الرائق: ٤٠٦/٧] فإن آجر إلخ أي فإن آجر المستعير المستعار فعطب أي هلك، ضمن المستعير؛ لأنه متعد بالتسليم إلى المستأجر ، فصار غاصباً، وإن شاء ضمن المستأجر؛ لأنه قبض ماله بغير إذنه، فإن ضمن المستعير لا يرجع على المستأجر؛ لأنه ملكه بالضمان وتبين أنه آجر ملك نفسه، وإن ضمن المستأجر يرجع على المستعير المؤجر إذا لم يعلم أنه كان عارية في يده، وإن علم فلا يرجع، كالمستأجر من الغاصب عالما بالغصب. رمز الحقائق: ٢٥٦/٢] فعطبت إلخ : أي هلكت وكذا إذا استهلكها المستأجر يتخير المعير في التضمين أيضاً، لكن إن اختار تضمين المستعير رجع على المستأجر وفي الهلاك لا يرجع، حموي عن المقدسي. (فتح) ويعير إلخ لكونه ملك المنفعة، فملك أن يملكها، قيد بـ"ما لا يختلف"، وهو الحمل والاستخدام والسكنى؛ لأن ما يختلف ليس له فيه أن يعير كاللبس والركوب لكن بشرط أن تكون مقيدة، أما لو كانت مطلقة كما لو استعار دابة للركوب أو ثوباً للبس، له أن يعيرهما، ويكون ذلك تعييناً للراكب واللابس، فإن ركب هو بعد ذلك، قال الإمام علي البزدوي: يكون ضامناً، وقال السرخسي وخواهرزاده لا يضمن كذا في "فتاوى قاضي خان"، وصحح الأول في "الكافي". [البحر الرائق: ٤٠٦/٧] ما لا يختلف إلخ سواء عين منتفعا أو لا، إلا أن يقول: لا تدفع إلى غيرك فإن دفع بعد النهي وهلك ضمن وأما ما يختلف به فله أن يعير إن لم يعين منتفعاً، فمن استعار دابة أو استأجرها مطلقاً بلا تقييد يحمل عليها ما شاء ويعير ويركب بنفسه ويركب غيره وأياً فعل تعين وضمن بغيره، وما في "البحر" عن "المحيط": استعار دابة ليركبها فركب وأركب غيره فعطبت ضمن نصف قيمتها معناه أنهما ركباها معاً؛ لأن سبب العطب ركوبهما معاً وأحدهما مأذون فيه فلهذا ضمن النصف، حتى لو أركب غيره فقط ضمن الكل، هذا ما ظهر لي ولم أر من نبه عليه. (فتح الله المعين) فلو قيدها إلخ: أي فلو قيد المعير المستعار بوقت كيوم أو شهر، أو منفعة كما إذا قال: اركب هذه الدابة، أو قيد بهما لا يجاوز عما سماه أي لا يجاوز المستعير عما سماه المعير من الوقت أو المنفعة أو منهما؛ لأنه تصرف في ملك الغير، فلا يجوز إلا على الوجه الذي أذن فيه من تقييد أو إطلاق. (مسكين، عيني) لا يتجاوز عما سماه إلخ : أشار بقوله : "لا يتجاوز" إلى أنه لا يتعدى المسمى، فأفاد أنه لابد أن تكون المخالفة إلى شر، فلو خالف إلى مثل المسمى بأن استعار دابة ليحمل عليها عشرة أقفزة من حنطة معينة فحمل عليها :
And it (the borrowed item) is not rented; meaning the borrowed item is not rented because rental is stronger because it is binding. So if he [the borrower] were to rent it, there would be the binding of what is non-binding (the loan) or the non-binding of what is binding (the rental). [al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 406/7] And it is not pledged like a deposit. If he rents it and it is destroyed, he is liable. And he (the borrower) may lend (to another) what does not vary with use. So if the borrower restricts it by a time or benefit or both, he must not exceed what he named. ... And also if the borrower rents it and it is destroyed, the lender may hold either the borrower or the lessee liable. ... The ruling on lending: because he owns the benefit, so he may grant ownership of it. It is restricted to 'what does not vary', which is carrying, service, and dwelling. ... If the lender specified a time or benefit, the borrower must not exceed it. The specification indicates that the deviation must be to something worse; if he deviates to something similar, it is not considered exceeding.
Source pages p. 122

Commentary
This passage combines several rulings related to 'ariyah. First, the borrower cannot rent out the borrowed item because rental is a binding contract while loan is non-binding; allowing rental would lead to inconsistency. Second, the borrower cannot pledge the item as collateral because that would be using another's property to secure one's debt. The borrower can, however, deposit (wadi'ah) the item with another, according to the mufta bihi view. Third, the borrower may lend the item to a third party if the benefit is not variable (e.g., carrying, service, dwelling). For variable benefits like riding or wearing, lending is only allowed if the original loan was unrestricted; if the borrower then also uses it himself, there is an intra-Hanafi dispute: al-Bazdawi holds him liable, while al-Sarakhsi and Khwaharzadeh do not. The commentary also discusses what happens if the borrower rents it out and it is destroyed: the owner can claim from either the borrower or the lessee, with rules on recourse. Finally, if the lender specifies a time or benefit, the borrower must adhere; exceeding the specification is only considered transgression if the deviation is to something worse than what was specified.

Key Terms
إجارة (ijarah): A binding hire contract for benefit.
رهن (rahn): Pledge as security for debt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school prohibit a borrower from renting the borrowed item?
A) Because rental requires a specific time period.
B) Because rental is a binding contract and the loan is non-binding.
C) Because the borrower does not have the item in his possession.
D) Because the owner may need the item back suddenly.

Key Takeaway
A borrower cannot impose a binding contract on a non-binding loan, so renting and pledging are prohibited.

Lending the Borrowed Item: Variable vs Non-Variable Benefits
Permissibility of lending borrowed items based on benefit type.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between variable and non-variable benefits in borrowed items and state when a borrower may lend to a third party.

Core Idea
A borrower may lend only benefits that do not vary with the user, like carriage; for variable benefits, lending is restricted.

The borrower has the right to use the borrowed item but not necessarily to transfer that right. The Hanafi school differentiates between benefits that are uniform regardless of the user (e.g., carrying loads) and those that vary (e.g., riding a horse). This lesson explores the rules for lending these benefits to others and the resulting liability disputes among Hanafi scholars.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories of benefits
The text divides benefits into 'what does not vary' (ma la yakhtalif) like carrying, service, dwelling, and 'what does vary' (ma yakhtalif) like riding or wearing.
Non-variable benefits are essentially the same for any user.
2
Rule for non-variable benefits
The borrower may lend these to another because the benefit is generic; the lender's permission for use covers any user.
This is unconditional unless the owner prohibits it.
3
Rule for variable benefits when loan is unrestricted
If the loan was unrestricted (mutlaq), the borrower may lend the item to another for a variable benefit like riding. This is considered a designation of the user.
The borrower must not then use it himself after lending? The text discusses liability if he also uses.
4
Intra-Hanafi dispute on liability
If the borrower lends a variable-benefit item (e.g., horse for riding) and then also rides it himself, there is a dispute: Imam al-Bazdawi says he becomes liable (damages), while al-Sarakhsi and Khwaharzadeh say he does not.
The mufta bihi according to al-Kafi is Bazdawi's view.
5
Apply the ruling to real cases
For example, a borrowed car for transportation (non-variable) can be lent to another; a borrowed dress for wearing (variable) requires caution.
Always check if the owner specified intended use.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا تؤجر أي ولا تؤجر العارية؛ لأن الإجارة أقوى؛ لأنها لازمة، فلو ملكها لزم لزوم ما لا يلزم، وهو العارية، أو عدم لزوم ما يلزم وهو الإجارة [البحر الرائق: ٤٠٦/٧] : ولا ترهن كالوديعة فإن آجر فعطبت ،ضمن ويعير ما لا يختلف بالمستعمل، فلو أي المستعير العارية المستعير المستعير قيدها بوقت أو منفعة أو بهما، لا يتجاوز عما سَمَّاه، أي المعير العارية كالشهر مثلا كركوب الدابة أي المستعير ولا ترهن لأن الرهن إيفاء وليس له أن يوفي دينه بمال غيره بغير إذنه، وله أن يودع على المفتى به، وهو المختار، وصحح بعضهم عدمه، ويتفرع عليه ما لو أرسلها على يد أجنبي، فهلكت يضمن على الثاني لا الأول، وسيأتي قريبا. [البحر الرائق: ٤٠٦/٧] فإن آجر إلخ أي فإن آجر المستعير المستعار فعطب أي هلك، ضمن المستعير؛ لأنه متعد بالتسليم إلى المستأجر ، فصار غاصباً، وإن شاء ضمن المستأجر؛ لأنه قبض ماله بغير إذنه، فإن ضمن المستعير لا يرجع على المستأجر؛ لأنه ملكه بالضمان وتبين أنه آجر ملك نفسه، وإن ضمن المستأجر يرجع على المستعير المؤجر إذا لم يعلم أنه كان عارية في يده، وإن علم فلا يرجع، كالمستأجر من الغاصب عالما بالغصب. رمز الحقائق: ٢٥٦/٢] فعطبت إلخ : أي هلكت وكذا إذا استهلكها المستأجر يتخير المعير في التضمين أيضاً، لكن إن اختار تضمين المستعير رجع على المستأجر وفي الهلاك لا يرجع، حموي عن المقدسي. (فتح) ويعير إلخ لكونه ملك المنفعة، فملك أن يملكها، قيد بـ"ما لا يختلف"، وهو الحمل والاستخدام والسكنى؛ لأن ما يختلف ليس له فيه أن يعير كاللبس والركوب لكن بشرط أن تكون مقيدة، أما لو كانت مطلقة كما لو استعار دابة للركوب أو ثوباً للبس، له أن يعيرهما، ويكون ذلك تعييناً للراكب واللابس، فإن ركب هو بعد ذلك، قال الإمام علي البزدوي: يكون ضامناً، وقال السرخسي وخواهرزاده لا يضمن كذا في "فتاوى قاضي خان"، وصحح الأول في "الكافي". [البحر الرائق: ٤٠٦/٧] ما لا يختلف إلخ سواء عين منتفعا أو لا، إلا أن يقول: لا تدفع إلى غيرك فإن دفع بعد النهي وهلك ضمن وأما ما يختلف به فله أن يعير إن لم يعين منتفعاً، فمن استعار دابة أو استأجرها مطلقاً بلا تقييد يحمل عليها ما شاء ويعير ويركب بنفسه ويركب غيره وأياً فعل تعين وضمن بغيره، وما في "البحر" عن "المحيط": استعار دابة ليركبها فركب وأركب غيره فعطبت ضمن نصف قيمتها معناه أنهما ركباها معاً؛ لأن سبب العطب ركوبهما معاً وأحدهما مأذون فيه فلهذا ضمن النصف، حتى لو أركب غيره فقط ضمن الكل، هذا ما ظهر لي ولم أر من نبه عليه. (فتح الله المعين) فلو قيدها إلخ: أي فلو قيد المعير المستعار بوقت كيوم أو شهر، أو منفعة كما إذا قال: اركب هذه الدابة، أو قيد بهما لا يجاوز عما سماه أي لا يجاوز المستعير عما سماه المعير من الوقت أو المنفعة أو منهما؛ لأنه تصرف في ملك الغير، فلا يجوز إلا على الوجه الذي أذن فيه من تقييد أو إطلاق. (مسكين، عيني) لا يتجاوز عما سماه إلخ : أشار بقوله : "لا يتجاوز" إلى أنه لا يتعدى المسمى، فأفاد أنه لابد أن تكون المخالفة إلى شر، فلو خالف إلى مثل المسمى بأن استعار دابة ليحمل عليها عشرة أقفزة من حنطة معينة فحمل عليها :
And it (the borrowed item) is not rented; meaning the borrowed item is not rented because rental is stronger because it is binding. So if he [the borrower] were to rent it, there would be the binding of what is non-binding (the loan) or the non-binding of what is binding (the rental). [al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 406/7] And it is not pledged like a deposit. If he rents it and it is destroyed, he is liable. And he (the borrower) may lend (to another) what does not vary with use. So if the borrower restricts it by a time or benefit or both, he must not exceed what he named. ... And also if the borrower rents it and it is destroyed, the lender may hold either the borrower or the lessee liable. ... The ruling on lending: because he owns the benefit, so he may grant ownership of it. It is restricted to 'what does not vary', which is carrying, service, and dwelling. ... If the lender specified a time or benefit, the borrower must not exceed it. The specification indicates that the deviation must be to something worse; if he deviates to something similar, it is not considered exceeding.
Source pages p. 122

Commentary
This passage combines several rulings related to 'ariyah. First, the borrower cannot rent out the borrowed item because rental is a binding contract while loan is non-binding; allowing rental would lead to inconsistency. Second, the borrower cannot pledge the item as collateral because that would be using another's property to secure one's debt. The borrower can, however, deposit (wadi'ah) the item with another, according to the mufta bihi view. Third, the borrower may lend the item to a third party if the benefit is not variable (e.g., carrying, service, dwelling). For variable benefits like riding or wearing, lending is only allowed if the original loan was unrestricted; if the borrower then also uses it himself, there is an intra-Hanafi dispute: al-Bazdawi holds him liable, while al-Sarakhsi and Khwaharzadeh do not. The commentary also discusses what happens if the borrower rents it out and it is destroyed: the owner can claim from either the borrower or the lessee, with rules on recourse. Finally, if the lender specifies a time or benefit, the borrower must adhere; exceeding the specification is only considered transgression if the deviation is to something worse than what was specified.

Key Terms
ما لا يختلف (ma la yakhtalif): Benefits that do not vary with the user, e.g., carrying load, service, dwelling.
تقيد (taqyid): Specification of time or benefit by the lender.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi view in the Hanafi school, if a borrower lends a borrowed horse (for riding) to another and then rides it himself, what is his liability?
A) He is not liable because the loan was unrestricted.
B) He is only liable if the horse is injured while he rides.
C) He is liable because lending specifies the user and his own use exceeds that.
D) He is liable only if the horse dies.

Key Takeaway
For variable benefits, the borrower may lend only if the original loan was unrestricted; the mufta bihi holds him liable if he then uses it himself.

Adhering to Specifications and Consequences of Deviation
Obligation to adhere to specifications in borrowed items.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rule that a borrower must adhere to any specifications of time or benefit made by the lender and identify when deviation leads to liability.

Core Idea
The borrower must not exceed the lender's specification; only deviation to a worse use is considered transgression.

When a lender specifies a particular time, benefit, or both, the borrower is bound by that. The Hanafi school further clarifies that only deviations that make the use worse than specified are considered harmful (darr). This lesson explores the rule and its practical application, including the nuance of 'similar' vs 'worse' usage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the specification
The lender may restrict the borrowed item to a specific time (e.g., one month) or benefit (e.g., only for riding) or both.
Specification is the lender's right; it limits the borrower's permission.
2
Rule: No exceeding the specification
The text states clearly: 'la yatajawazu 'amma sammahu' — he must not exceed what he named.
This applies to time, benefit, or both.
3
Understanding 'deviation to worse'
The commentary explains that exceeding is only prohibited if the deviation is to a worse (sharr) use. If the deviation is to a similar (mithl) use, it is not considered exceeding.
This nuance prevents trivial litigation.
4
Example of worse deviation
If a horse is borrowed for riding (specified benefit), using it for heavy pulling may be worse. The borrower would be liable for damage.
The example in the text: borrowing a donkey to carry 10 measures of a specified grain, then carrying 10 measures of a different grain (similar)? Actually text cuts off.
5
Consequences of exceeding
If the borrower exceeds the specification in a way that causes damage, he becomes liable (dam) because he acted without permission.
This is part of the general principle of transgression (ta'addi).

Source Text

Key Terms
مثل (mithl): Similar; deviation to a similar use is not transgression.
شر (sharr): Worse; deviation to worse use is transgression and may incur liability.

Prohibition of Pledging a Loaned Item and Liability upon Rental
Ruling on borrower's unauthorized disposition and liability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on a borrower pledging a loaned item and explain the liability when a borrower rents out the loaned item and it is destroyed.

Core Idea
A borrower may not pledge a loaned item; if he rents it out and it is destroyed, he becomes liable for its value.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq addresses two key issues in the law of loans ('ariyah). First, a borrower cannot pledge the borrowed item because that would use another's property to secure his own debt without permission. Second, if the borrower rents out the item and it perishes, the borrower becomes liable as a usurper, though the lender may alternatively hold the lessee liable. The passage also notes an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether the borrower may deposit the item with a third party.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts and rulings
Read the opening phrase: 'Do not pledge it like a trust'. This states a prohibition (haram) on the borrower pledging the loaned item. Then note the consequence: 'If he rents it out and it is destroyed, he guarantees.' Identify the two distinct ruling scenarios.
The text treats pledging and renting out as separate unauthorized acts.
2
Understand the reason for the prohibition
The commentary explains: pledging is a fulfillment of debt; the borrower has no right to use another's property to pay his debt without permission. This establishes the legal basis for the prohibition.
The borrower is a trustee (amin), not an owner; any use beyond permission breaches trust.
3
Analyze the dispute on depositing
The text mentions that the borrower may deposit the item according to the mufta bihi view, though some scholars reject this. Understand the practical difference: if the borrower deposits and the item is lost, on the first view he is not liable; on the second he is liable.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf; the preferred view (mufta bihi) is that depositing is permissible.
4
Apply the liability rules for rental
If the borrower rents out the item and it is destroyed, the lender may claim damages from either the borrower (as usurper) or the lessee (as possessor without permission). Trace how each option affects subsequent recourse between the parties.
The borrower's unauthorized delivery to the lessee constitutes transgression (ta'addi), making the borrower a guarantor.
5
Consider analogous cases
The text draws an analogy with the lessee from a usurper: if the lessee knew the item was borrowed, he cannot claim from the borrower. Similarly, if the lessee consumes the item, the lender has the same options. Use this to solidify the principle.
Knowledge of the borrower's lack of ownership affects the lessee's right of recourse.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا ترهن كالوديعة فإن آجر فعطبت ضمن، ولا ترهن لأن الرهن إيفاء وليس له أن يوفي دينه بمال غيره بغير إذنه، وله أن يودع على المفتى به، وهو المختار، وصحح بعضهم عدمه، ويتفرع عليه ما لو أرسلها على يد أجنبي، فهلكت يضمن على الثاني لا الأول، وسيأتي قريبا. [البحر الرائق: ٤٠٦/٧] فإن آجر إلخ أي فإن آجر المستعير المستعار فعطب أي هلك، ضمن المستعير؛ لأنه متعد بالتسليم إلى المستأجر، فصار غاصباً، وإن شاء ضمن المستأجر؛ لأنه قبض ماله بغير إذنه، فإن ضمن المستعير لا يرجع على المستأجر؛ لأنه ملكه بالضمان وتبين أنه آجر ملك نفسه، وإن ضمن المستأجر يرجع على المستعير المؤجر إذا لم يعلم أنه كان عارية في يده، وإن علم فلا يرجع، كالمستأجر من الغاصب عالما بالغصب. رمز الحقائق: ٢٥٦/٢] فعطبت إلخ : أي هلكت وكذا إذا استهلكها المستأجر يتخير المعير في التضمين أيضاً، لكن إن اختار تضمين المستعير رجع على المستأجر وفي الهلاك لا يرجع، حموي عن المقدسي. (فتح)
Do not pledge it like a trust. If he rents it out and it is destroyed, he guarantees. The statement: 'Do not pledge it because pledging is fulfillment of debt, and he has no right to fulfill his debt with another's property without his permission. He may deposit it according to the mufta bihi view, which is the chosen one, and some have corrected its absence. Branched from this is if he sends it via a third party and it is destroyed, he guarantees according to the second view, not the first, as will come soon. [al-Bahr al-Raiq 7/406] The statement: 'If he rents it out' etc. means if the borrower rents out the loaned item and it is destroyed, the borrower guarantees because he transgressed by handing it over to the lessee, becoming a usurper. If he wishes, he can make the lessee guarantee because he took property without permission. If the borrower guarantees, he cannot claim from the lessee because he owned it by guarantee and it becomes clear he rented out his own property. If the lessee guarantees, he may claim against the borrower/lessor if he did not know it was a loan in his possession; if he knew, he cannot claim, like the lessee from a usurper knowingly. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2/256) The statement: 'and it is destroyed' etc. means it perished. Similarly, if the lessee consumes it, the lender has the option to claim guarantee from either. If he chooses to claim from the borrower, the borrower may then claim from the lessee; in the case of destruction, he cannot claim back. (Hamwi from al-Maqdisi, Fath)
Source pages p. 123

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq on the law of loans ('ariyah). The first ruling prohibits a borrower from pledging a loaned item (like a trust) because pledging is a form of fulfilling a debt, and a borrower may not use another's property to pay his debt without permission. The mufta bihi position allows the borrower to deposit the item with someone else. The second part addresses the case where a borrower rents out the loaned item and it perishes. The borrower is liable because he exceeds his permission, effectively becoming a usurper (ghasib). Alternatively, the lender may hold the lessee liable. If the lender chooses the borrower, the borrower cannot recover from the lessee; if the lender chooses the lessee, the lessee may recover from the borrower unless the lessee knew the item was borrowed. This is analogous to leasing from a usurper with knowledge.

Key Terms
عارية (‘āriyah): A loan of a tangible item for use without compensation
رهن (rahn): Pledge; giving an item as security for a debt
ضمان (ḍamān): Liability; guarantee; obligation to compensate for loss

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, if a borrower rents out a loaned item and it is destroyed, who may the lender claim against?
A) Only the borrower
B) Only the lessee
C) Either the borrower or the lessee
D) Neither, because it is a loan

Key Takeaway
A borrower is a trustee but becomes liable if he exceeds permission, such as by renting out the item; the lender may claim from either the borrower or the lessee.

The Rule on Loaning Items Not Varying by Use
Ruling on loaning items that do not vary by use

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for a borrower lending borrowed items and identify which items may be loaned out.

Core Idea
A borrower may loan out only items whose usufruct does not change by the user.

This lesson explains the Hanafi ruling on a borrower's right to lend borrowed items. The key distinction is whether the item's utility varies with the user. Items like carrying, service, and dwelling are examples where the usufruct remains the same regardless of who uses them. Clothing and riding, however, vary with the user, so they cannot be lent by the borrower unless the loan was unrestricted.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act being ruled upon
The ruling concerns the borrower lending the borrowed item to a third party. The default permissibility depends on the nature of the item.
This is a sub-ruling within the contract of ariyah (loan).
2
Distinguish items that vary by use from those that do not
Items that do not vary include carrying (حمْل), service (استخدام), and dwelling (سكنى). Items that vary include clothing (لبس) and riding (ركوب). Classification determines whether the borrower may lend.
The variation refers to physical wear or change in utility from different users.
3
Apply the condition of restriction
If the original loan was restricted to a specific user (e.g., 'only you may ride'), the borrower cannot lend. If unrestricted, he may lend, but doing so specifies the new user.
Unrestricted means the lender did not designate a particular user; the borrower effectively has the right to use but also to delegate.
4
Note the consequence of lending in an unrestricted case
When the borrower lends, the new user becomes specified (تعيين), and the borrower is then prohibited from using it himself without becoming liable for damages.
This is a key Hanafi principle: the act of lending changes the legal status of the borrower's own permission.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويعير ما لا يختلف بالمستعمل، ويعير إلخ لكونه ملك المنفعة، فملك أن يملكها، قيد بـ"ما لا يختلف"، وهو الحمل والاستخدام والسكنى؛ لأن ما يختلف ليس له فيه أن يعير كاللبس والركوب لكن بشرط أن تكون مقيدة، أما لو كانت مطلقة كما لو استعار دابة للركوب أو ثوباً للبس، له أن يعيرهما، ويكون ذلك تعييناً للراكب واللابس، فإن ركب هو بعد ذلك، قال الإمام علي البزدوي: يكون ضامناً، وقال السرخسي وخواهرزاده لا يضمن كذا في "فتاوى قاضي خان"، وصحح الأول في "الكافي". [البحر الرائق: ٤٠٦/٧] ما لا يختلف إلخ سواء عين منتفعا أو لا، إلا أن يقول: لا تدفع إلى غيرك فإن دفع بعد النهي وهلك ضمن وأما ما يختلف به فله أن يعير إن لم يعين منتفعاً، فمن استعار دابة أو استأجرها مطلقاً بلا تقييد يحمل عليها ما شاء ويعير ويركب بنفسه ويركب غيره وأياً فعل تعين وضمن بغيره، وما في "البحر" عن "المحيط": استعار دابة ليركبها فركب وأركب غيره فعطبت ضمن نصف قيمتها معناه أنهما ركباها معاً؛ لأن سبب العطب ركوبهما معاً وأحدهما مأذون فيه فلهذا ضمن النصف، حتى لو أركب غيره فقط ضمن الكل، هذا ما ظهر لي ولم أر من نبه عليه. (فتح الله المعين)
And he may loan out what does not vary by use. The statement: 'he may loan out' etc. because he owns the usufruct, so he may transfer ownership of it. It is restricted to 'what does not vary', which is carrying, service, and dwelling; because what does vary, he may not loan out, like clothing and riding, but on condition that they are restricted. However, if they are unrestricted, as if he borrows a riding animal or a garment for wearing, he may loan them out, and that becomes a specification of the rider or wearer. If he then rides himself, Imam Ali al-Bazdawi said he becomes liable; al-Sarakhsi and Khawaharzada said he is not liable, as in Fatawa Qadi Khan, and the first is corrected in al-Kafi. [al-Bahr al-Raiq 7/406] 'What does not vary' etc. whether or not he specifies a beneficiary, unless he says: do not give to others. If he gives after a prohibition and it is destroyed, he is liable. As for what varies, he may loan it out if he has not specified a beneficiary. So whoever borrows an animal or hires it absolutely without restriction may load whatever he wishes, loan it out, ride himself, and let others ride. Whichever he does, it becomes specified and he is liable for others. In al-Bahr from al-Muhit: someone borrowed an animal to ride, rode and gave another to ride, and it was destroyed: he guarantees half its value, meaning they both rode together; because the cause of destruction was both riding, and one was permitted, so he guarantees half. If he only had another ride, he guarantees the whole. This is what appeared to me, and I have not seen anyone point it out. (Fath Allah al-Mu'in)
Source pages p. 123

Commentary
This passage elaborates the matn ruling that a borrower may loan out items 'that do not vary by use', meaning items like a beast of burden for carrying goods, a servant for service, or a house for dwelling. Items that vary by use, such as clothing (which conforms to the wearer's body) or a riding animal (which endures the rider's weight and movement), may not be loaned out by the borrower, but only if the loan was restricted as to the user. If the loan was unrestricted (e.g., borrowing a horse for riding without specifying who rides), the borrower may let others ride, but doing so specifies the user, and the borrower may no longer ride himself without becoming liable. There is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: al-Bazdawi holds that if the borrower loans out a restricted item, he becomes liable if he then uses it himself; al-Sarakhsi disagrees. The mufta bihi is al-Bazdawi's view. The passage also discusses partial liability when two people ride together, one permitted, one not.

Key Terms
ما لا يختلف بالمستعمل (mā lā yakhtalifu bi al-musta‘mal): Items that do not change or get damaged by the specific user; e.g., carrying loads, service, dwelling
تعيين (ta‘yīn): Specification of the user by actual use; once specified, the borrower cannot change the user without permission

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following borrowed items may a borrower loan out according to the Hanafi school?
A) A horse for riding, if unrestricted
B) A house for dwelling, even if restricted
C) A garment for wearing, if unrestricted
D) A truck for carrying goods, even if restricted

Key Takeaway
A borrower may only lend borrowed items whose usufruct is unaffected by the identity of the user.

Specification (Ta‘yīn) and Liability in Unrestricted Loans
Intra-Hanafi dispute on liability and partial liability scenario

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi concept of ta‘yīn and describe the intra-Hanafi dispute on a borrower's liability when using a borrowed item after lending it.

Core Idea
Lending an unrestricted item specifies the user; the borrower becomes liable if he then uses it himself.

When a borrower lends an item borrowed under an unrestricted loan, the act of lending designates a specific user (ta‘yīn). This restricts the borrower's own right to use the item. If he subsequently uses it, he becomes a transgressor and is liable for damages. Among Hanafi scholars, there is a disagreement: Imam Ali al-Bazdawi holds he is liable, while al-Sarakhsi and Khawaharzada argue he is not. The relied-upon view is al-Bazdawi's, as corrected in al-Kafi.

Guided Path
1
Understand that lending an unrestricted item specifies the user
By lending to another, the borrower effectively transfers his own right of use to the new user. This act makes the new user the specified beneficiary.
This specification is a consequence of the borrower's action, not the lender's original permission.
2
Identify the prohibition on the borrower's use after specification
Once a specific user is designated, the borrower no longer has permission to use the item himself.
Any use by the borrower after that is considered a transgression (ta‘addī).
3
Recognize the intra-Hanafi dispute on liability
Al-Bazdawi: the borrower is liable (ḍāmin) if he uses it after lending. Al-Sarakhsi and Khawaharzada: he is not liable because the original permission still exists.
The dispute is about whether the original permission is revoked by the borrower's own lending.
4
Determine the mufta bihi position
The mufta bihi is al-Bazdawi's view, as corrected in al-Kafi. This means that in practice, the borrower is liable.
This tarjih is indicated by the phrase 'cured in al-Kafi'.
5
Apply to the partial liability scenario
If the borrower and the new user both ride together, and the animal is destroyed, the borrower guarantees half, because the cause (riding) is shared between a permitted user and a transgressor.
If the borrower only lets another ride, he guarantees the full value.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Borrower’s Exceeding Restrictions: When Liability Arises
Ruling on borrower exceeding restrictions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rule on borrower's liability when exceeding restrictions set by the lender and distinguish between violations to worse, equal, or better conditions.

Core Idea
Only violations to a worse condition incur liability; equal or better do not.

This passage from al-Muqaddimah al-Quduriyya and its sharh in al-Bahr al-Raiq clarifies a nuanced rule in the law of ariyah (loan). It shows that not every violation of the lender's restriction makes the borrower liable; only those that result in a worse or more harmful outcome. This precision protects borrowers from liability for harmless or even beneficial changes, while still safeguarding the lender's property rights.

Guided Path
1
Identify the restriction
First, note what the lender specified – time (e.g., a month), benefit (e.g., riding), or both. This restriction defines the borrower's authorised use.
The restriction can be explicit or implied by the nature of the loan.
2
Assess the violation
Compare the borrower's actual use to the specified use. Determine if the change is to something worse (more harmful), equal, or better (less harmful).
Worse means more harmful to the borrowed item, e.g., heavier load, longer duration.
3
Apply the liability rule
If the violation is to a worse condition, the borrower is liable (damān). If equal or better, he is not liable, because the restriction is only meaningful when it benefits the lender.
An exception arises when the weight is equal but volume larger – then there is ikhtilaf.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Al-Nihaya holds liability when the weight is same but the volume is larger (e.g., barley vs wheat). Al-Walwaliji corrects to non-liability. The relied-upon view is that of al-Nihaya.
This shows that even within a school, fine-grained adjustments occur.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فلو قيدها بوقت أو منفعة أو بهما، لا يتجاوز عما سَمَّاه، أي المعير العارية كالشهر مثلا كركوب الدابة أي المستعير فلو قيدها إلخ: أي فلو قيد المعير المستعار بوقت كيوم أو شهر، أو منفعة كما إذا قال: اركب هذه الدابة، أو قيد بهما لا يجاوز عما سماه أي لا يجاوز المستعير عما سماه المعير من الوقت أو المنفعة أو منهما؛ لأنه تصرف في ملك الغير، فلا يجوز إلا على الوجه الذي أذن فيه من تقييد أو إطلاق. (مسكين، عيني) لا يتجاوز عما سماه إلخ : أشار بقوله : "لا يتجاوز" إلى أنه لا يتعدى المسمى، فأفاد أنه لابد أن تكون المخالفة إلى شر، فلو خالف إلى مثل المسمى بأن استعار دابة ليحمل عليها عشرة أقفزة من حنطة معينة فحمل عليها هذا القدر من حنطة أخرى، أو ليحمل عليها حنطة نفسه، فحمل عليها حنطة غيره، أو خالف إلى خير من المسمى بأن حمل هذا القدر من الشعير لا يكون ضامناً؛ لأنه إنما يعتبر من تقييده ما يكون مفيداً حتى لو سمى مقداراً . الحنطة وزناً، فحمل مثل ذلك الوزن من الشعير يضمن؛ لأنه يأخذ من ظهر الدابة أكثر مما تأخذه الحنطة، كذا في "النهاية"، وصحح الولوالجي عدم الضمان. [البحر الرائق: ٤٠٧/٧]
If he restricts it by time, benefit, or both, he may not exceed what was specified. (Explanation: the lender of the loan, e.g., a month, or riding the animal, etc. the borrower.) The statement: 'If he restricts it' etc. means: if the lender restricts the loaned item by time like a day or month, or benefit as when he says: 'Ride this animal', or restricts by both, the borrower may not exceed what was specified, because it is an action in another's property, so it is only permissible in the manner permitted, whether restricted or absolute. (Miskin, Ayni) The statement: 'he may not exceed what was specified' etc. indicates that he does not go beyond it. It shows that the violation must be to something worse. If he violates to something equal, e.g., he borrows an animal to carry ten qafiz of a specific wheat, and he carries that amount of other wheat, or to carry his own wheat but carries another's wheat, or violates to something better by carrying that amount of barley, he is not liable, because only restrictive conditions that are beneficial are considered. If he specifies a weight of wheat and carries the same weight of barley, he is liable because it takes more from the animal's back than wheat. (al-Nihaya) And al-Walwaliji corrected non-liability. (al-Bahr al-Raiq 7/407)
Source pages p. 123

Commentary
This passage explains the matn ruling that the borrower must not exceed the lender's restrictions of time or use. The commentary first clarifies the words: 'if he restricts' refers to the lender, and 'he may not exceed' refers to the borrower. The key principle is that a violation that results in something equal or better than specified does not incur liability, because the restriction is only meaningful if it is beneficial. For example, if the lender specifies a type of wheat, the borrower may carry an equivalent amount of other wheat or even barley (which is lighter and less harmful to the animal). However, if the specified wheat was by weight, and the borrower carries an equal weight of barley, the volume may be larger, causing more strain, so he is liable. There is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: al-Walwaliji holds non-liability, but the relied-upon view is liability as per al-Nihaya.

Key Terms
مخالفة إلى شر (mukhālafa ilā sharr): Violation to something worse or more harmful than specified
عارية (āriya): Loan of an item for benefit without charge
ضمان (damān): Liability for compensation

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Carrying the same weight of barley instead of wheat, when the weight is the same but volume is larger.
B) Carrying the same weight of a different type of wheat as specified.
C) Returning the borrowed item earlier than agreed.
D) Using the borrowed item for a shorter time than permitted.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a borrower is only liable for violating the lender's restriction if the violation results in a worse (more harmful) condition; equal or better changes are permissible without liability.

Unrestricted Loan and Loan of Consumables as Qard
Rulings on unrestricted loans and loan of dirhams, foodstuffs etc. being qard

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between a valid 'ariyah and a qard when loaning consumable items, and state the ruling on unrestricted loans.

Core Idea
A loan of consumable items is qard because benefit requires consumption of the substance.

In this passage, we learn two key rulings from Hanafi fiqh. First, if a loan is unrestricted, the borrower may use it in any permissible way. Second, when the loaned items are consumables like money or food, the transaction is legally a qard (loan for consumption) rather than a pure 'ariyah. This distinction affects liability and ownership.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
The passage states two independent rulings: (a) unrestricted loans and (b) loan of certain items being qard. First, note the full legal unit: the matn gives both rulings, and the commentary expands each.
The rulings are connected by the theme of when a loan changes legal nature.
2
Analyse the unrestricted loan ruling
Examine the matn: 'If he gives it absolutely, he may benefit in any type at any time.' Understand that the borrower can use the item in any permissible way unless specified. Even if specified, he may deviate to something equal or better.
This is for non-consumable items; the borrower does not own the substance.
3
Examine the conversion to qard
Focus on the second part: loans of gold, silver, measured, weighed, and counted items are qard. Understand the reasoning: these items are typically consumed when used, so the borrower must own the substance, making it a qard.
The borrower becomes liable to return the like (mithl) if lost before use.
4
Note the exceptions
Identify exceptions: if the loan is for a specific non-consumptive purpose (e.g., decoration), it remains 'ariyah. Also, loan of an arrow is not qard because its use is akin to destruction. Another exception is joviality indicating ibaha (permission).
These exceptions show the ruling is based on the underlying purpose.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

[البحر الرائق: ٤٠٧/٧] وتصح عارية السهم ولا يضمن؛ لأن الرمي يجري مجرى الهلاك "درر" عن "الصيرفية". (فتح) قرض فيضمن بهلاكها قبل الانتفاع كما هو حكم القرض، وإنما كان كذلك؛ لأن الإعارة تمليك المنفعة، ولا ينتفع بهذه الأمور إلا باستهلاك عينها، ولا يملك استهلاكها إلا إذا ملكها، فاقتضت تمليك عينها ضرورة، وذلك بالهبة أو القرض والقرض أدناهما؛ لكونه موجباً لرد المثل. (درر، فتح
And if he gives it absolutely, he may benefit in any type at any time. And the loan of the two precious metals (dirhams and dinars), and what is measured, weighed, and counted is a loan (qard). The statement: 'If he gives it absolutely' etc. means: if the lender gives the loan absolutely by not restricting it by time or benefit, the borrower may benefit from the loaned item in any type at any time. For example, if he borrows a riding animal for riding or a garment for wearing, he may wear and ride himself, and he may also (before he wears or rides) give to others to wear or ride. Then if he gives to others, he cannot ride himself afterwards according to the correct view, because it becomes specified by the act, so its violation is transgression. This is mentioned in al-Kafi. Then in every place where it is restricted by the specified, he may violate to something better or equal, as when he says: 'Carry this wheat on this animal', he may carry its like or less harmful. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2/257) And the loan of the two precious metals: dirhams and dinars; measured items like wheat and barley; weighed items like gold, silver, and honey; counted items like walnuts and eggs, is a loan (qard). They said this is if the loan is absolute. But if the purpose is specified, e.g., a money changer borrows dirhams to decorate his shop or to calibrate a scale, then it is not a qard. (Miskin) The measured etc. means what cannot be benefited from except by consuming the substance. Even if he says: 'I lend you this bowl of tharid (bread soaked in broth)', he takes and eats it, he owes its like or value, and it is a qard, unless there is joviality between them, then it indicates permission (ibaha). As in al-Bahr from al-Khulasa. (al-Bahr al-Raiq 7/407) And the loan of an arrow is valid and he is not liable, because shooting is like destruction. (Durar from al-Sayrafiyya, Fath) It is a qard, so he is liable if it perishes before using, as is the rule of qard. This is because loan is ownership of usufruct, and one cannot benefit from these things except by consuming their substance, and one cannot consume them unless he owns them. So it necessitates ownership of the substance, which is via gift or loan, and loan is the lesser because it requires return of the like. (Durar, Fath)
Source pages p. 124

Commentary
This passage covers two related rulings from the matn. First: if the loan is unrestricted, the borrower may use the item in any permissible way at any time. However, if he specifies an actual user by lending it to another, he himself cannot use it thereafter. He may deviate to something equal or better. Second: loan of items that are typically consumed (like money, foodstuffs, etc.) is legally treated as a qard (loan for consumption), because the only way to benefit is to consume them. The borrower becomes owner of the substance and must return the like. There is an exception if the loan is for a specific non-consumptive purpose (e.g., using dirhams for decoration). Also, loan of an arrow is not qard because it is used by shooting (almost like destruction).

Key Terms
قرض (qarḍ): Loan for consumption where the borrower owns the substance and must return the like
ثمنين (thamanayn): The two precious metals: gold (dinars) and silver (dirhams)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the loan of dirhams (silver coins) considered a qard rather than 'ariyah?
A) Because dirhams are not beneficial
B) Because the only way to benefit from dirhams is to spend them, which consumes the substance
C) Because the lender intends to give them away
D) Because the borrower must return the same coins

Key Takeaway
Loan of consumables is always qard in Hanafi fiqh, making the borrower liable to return the like.

Loan of Land for Building or Planting: Valid but Revocable
Ruling on lending land for building or planting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on lending land for construction or cultivation and explain the consequences of revocation.

Core Idea
A loan of land for building/planting is valid but revocable; the borrower must remove structures at his own cost.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq addresses a practical scenario: a lender allows someone to build a structure or plant trees on his land. While such a loan is valid, it does not become binding. The lender retains the right to revoke, and the borrower must then remove what he placed, unless the lender chooses to compensate to avoid damage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its validity
First, confirm that the loan (i‘ārah) of land for building or planting is valid (sahīh) because the usufruct is known (ma‘lūm).
The validity is derived from the permissibility of leasing the same land.
2
Understand the lender's right to revoke
The lender may revoke the loan at any time, as ‘āriyah is a non-binding (ghayr lāzim) contract.
This is a key characteristic of ‘ariyah in the Hanafi school.
3
Determine the consequences of revocation
Upon revocation, the borrower must remove (qal‘) the building or trees at his own expense. However, if removal would damage the land, the lender may instead take the building/trees at their value as removed (i.e., salvage value) and compensate the borrower.
The option to pay value is to prevent harm (ḍarar) to the land.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن أعار أرضا للبناء أو للغرس صح، ويكلف قلعهما، وله أن يرجع. وإن أعار إلخ: أي إن أعار رجل أرضا للبناء أو للغرس أي لغرس الشجر صح؛ لأن منفعتها معلومة، ويجوز إجارتها، فكذا إعارتها، بل أولى لكونها تبرعا. رمز الحقائق: ٢٥٧/٢] وله أن يرجع أي وللمعير أن يرجع عن العارية؛ لأنها غير لازمة. (عيني) ويكلف قلعهما: أي ويكلف المعير المستعير قلعهما أي قلع البناء والغرس؛ لأنه شاغل أرضه ملكه، فيؤمر بالتفريغ إلا إذا شاء أن يأخذهما بقيمتهما فيما إذا كانت الأرض تستضر بالقلع، فحينئذ يضمن له قيمتهما مقلوعين، • بقاء
And if he loans land for building or for planting, it is valid. He may demand their removal, and he may revoke. The statement: 'if he loans land' etc. means: if a man loans land for building or for planting i.e. for planting trees, it is valid, because its usufruct is known, and leasing it is permissible, so likewise lending it, indeed more so being a gratuitous act. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2/257) And he may revoke: i.e. the lender may revoke the loan because it is non-binding. (Ayni) And he may demand their removal: i.e. the lender may demand that the borrower remove them, i.e., remove the building and planting, because they occupy his land. He is ordered to vacate, unless he wishes to take them at their value when the land is damaged by removal, then he must guarantee their value as uprooted. • remains
Source pages p. 124

Commentary
This passage addresses the loan of land for building or planting trees. Such a loan is valid because the usufruct is known and can be leased, making it even more suitable for a gratuitous loan. However, the lender retains the right to revoke the loan at any time, as 'ariyah is not a binding contract. If he revokes, he can demand that the borrower remove structures or trees. If removal would damage the land, the lender may instead take the structures/trees at their value as removed (i.e., the value of the materials), compensating the borrower. The final word 'remains' likely refers to a note about continuing possession.

Key Terms
تعير (ta‘yīr): Loan of land for building or planting
قلع (qal‘): Removal of structures or trees from the land

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a lender loans land for planting trees, can he revoke the loan and demand removal of the trees?
A) No, because the trees are a long-term investment
B) Yes, but he must pay the value of the trees if removal damages the land
C) Yes, and the borrower must remove at his own expense always
D) No, because the loan becomes binding once trees are planted

Key Takeaway
A loan of land for building or planting is valid but revocable; the borrower must remove structures at his own expense unless the lender opts to compensate for land damage.

Aariyah of Fungibles Is Qard
Ruling that aariyah of consumables is a loan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four categories of fungible items whose aariyah is treated as qard and explain the legal consequence of ownership transfer.

Core Idea
Aariyah of consumable fungibles transfers ownership; borrower must return the like.

This short passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq draws a sharp line: lending a consumable fungible (money, grain, gold, eggs) as aariyah is not aariyah at all — it is qard. The reason is simple: aariyah only transfers usufruct, but using these items consumes their substance. Therefore, the law reclassifies the contract as a loan, making the borrower liable to return the exact same type and quantity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
The passage contains two distinct rules: first, an unrestricted aariyah grants the borrower complete freedom of use; second, aariyah of the listed fungible items is legally a qard.
The first part is a condition; the second is the main ruling.
2
Parse the four categories
List the four types: al-thamanayn (dirhams and dinars), al-makil (volume-measured), al-mawzun (weighed), al-ma'dud (counted). Each category represents items typically consumed by use.
These are the mithliyyat (fungibles) in Hanafi terminology.
3
Understand the legal transformation
Understand why aariyah becomes qard: aariyah only permits use without transferring ownership of the substance. For consumables, use requires consumption, so ownership must transfer. Hence, the contract is treated as a loan (qard), where ownership of the substitute transfers and the borrower must return the like (mithl).
This is a rule of istihsan, preserving the parties' intent while ensuring legal validity.
4
Apply to a scenario
Take a practical case: A lends B a basket of apples (ma'dud) as aariyah so B can sell them. B consumes them. The aariyah is qard, so B must return the value or like apples, not the original basket.
Liability attaches from receipt, like a loan.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن أطلق له أن ينتفع أي نوع في أي وقت شاء. وعارية الثمنين والمكيل والموزون والمعدود قرض.
If the lender gives unrestricted permission for the borrower to benefit in any way at any time. And the aariyah of dirhams and dinars (thamanain), and of measured items (makil), and of weighed items (mawzun), and of counted items (ma'dud) is a qard (loan).
Source pages p. 124

Commentary
This passage states two rulings. First, unrestricted aariyah allows the borrower any use at any time. Second, lending items consumed by use—like money, food grains, metals, eggs—is legally a qard, not aariyah. The reason is that aariyah transfers usufruct without ownership of substance; but these items require consumption for use, necessitating ownership transfer through a loan. Thus, the borrower must return the like (mithl) and is liable from receipt.

Key Terms
الثمنين (al-thamanayn): The two price items: dirhams and dinars (silver and gold coins)
المكيل (al-makil): Items measured by volume, e.g. wheat, barley
الموزون (al-mawzun): Items weighed, e.g. gold, silver, honey
المعدود (al-ma'dud): Items counted individually, e.g. walnuts, eggs

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, lending a measured item (makil) as aariyah is considered:
A) Valid aariyah with no guarantee for the borrower
B) A qard, and the borrower must return the same quantity
C) A prohibited transaction
D) Valid only if the borrower returns the exact same item

Key Takeaway
Aariyah of fungible consumables is legally a qard, requiring return of the like and liability from receipt.

Validity and Revocation of Land Aariyah
Ruling on validity and revocation of land aariyah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on lending land for building or planting and explain the consequences of revocation, including the exception for compensation.

Core Idea
Lending land is valid like renting, but revocable; removal is required unless the lender pays damages.

This lesson examines a concise ruling from Kanz al-Daqa'iq on lending land for construction or agriculture. The author establishes validity through qiyas on rental contracts and then clarifies the lender's right to revoke, the borrower's duty to remove, and a special option for the lender to pay compensation when removal would damage the land. Understanding this ruling clarifies how Hanafi fiqh balances property rights with the gratuitous nature of aariyah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
The passage gives a primary ruling (validity) and a secondary set (consequences after revocation). Separate them.
2
Analyze the qiyas argument
Why is aariyah valid? Because its benefit is known and renting is permissible; lending, being charitable, is even more fitting. Trace the logical analogy.
Qiyas jaliy: asl = ijara, far' = aariyah, illa = known benefit and permissibility
3
Understand the non-binding nature
Aariyah is ghayr lazim – the lender may revoke at any time. Recognize that this distinguishes it from binding contracts like ijara.
4
Apply revocation consequences
Borrower must remove buildings/trees at own cost (qal'). Note the exception: if removal harms the land, lender may opt to pay the value of the structures as uprooted, and then borrower is not forced to remove.
The phrase 'إلا إذا شاء أن يأخذهما بقيمتهما' introduces the exception.
5
Reflect on the balance
The ruling protects the owner's right to reclaim land while sparing the land from unnecessary damage through a compensation option. This is a practical application of istihsan.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن أعار أرضا للبناء أو للغرس صح؛ لأن منفعتها معلومة، ويجوز إجارتها، فكذا إعارتها، بل أولى لكونها تبرعا. وله أن يرجع؛ لأنها غير لازمة. ويكلف قلعهما؛ لأنه شاغل أرضه ملكه، فيؤمر بالتفريغ إلا إذا شاء أن يأخذهما بقيمتهما فيما إذا كانت الأرض تستضر بالقلع، فحينئذ يضمن له قيمتهما مقلوعين.
And if one lends land for building or for planting, it is valid, because its benefit is known, and it is permissible to rent it, so likewise is lending it—indeed even more so because it is gratuitous. And the lender may revoke it, because it is not binding. And the borrower is obliged to remove (the building or plantation), because they occupy the lender's property; he is ordered to vacate unless the lender chooses to take them at their value, in which case he guarantees to pay their value as uprooted.
Source pages p. 124

Commentary
This passage discusses lending land for construction or planting. First, it declares validity, analogizing to ijara (rent) which is permissible; aariyah is even more so as it is charitable. Second, the lender may revoke the aariyah at any time because it is not a binding contract (ghayr lazim). Third, the borrower must remove structures or trees, as they occupy the owner's land. However, if removal damages the land, the lender may optionally purchase them at their value as uprooted, and the borrower is entitled to that value.

Key Terms
القلع (al-qal'): Removal or uprooting of a structure or tree from the land
التبرع (al-tabarru'): Gratuitous act; aariyah is a charitable contract

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When does the lender have an option to take the building/trees at their value?
A) Always, at the lender's will
B) Only when removal damages the land
C) When the borrower consents
D) Never, only removal is allowed

Key Takeaway
Lending land for construction or planting is valid and revocable; the borrower must remove improvements unless the lender compensates to avoid land damage.

Guarantee on Revocation and Special Rules for Planted Land
Dispute with Zufar over guarantee and rules for land planted

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi majority imposes guarantee when the lender revokes before a specified time, and distinguish Zufar's objection within the madhhab.

Core Idea
Specifying a time in aariyah creates reliance; revoking before it is deceptive and triggers guarantee.

Aariyah (gratuitous loan) is normally non-binding – the lender may revoke at any time without liability. However, when a specific time is promised, the borrower relies on that promise. This lesson examines the majority Hanafi view that early revocation then incurs guarantee for the deficiency, and the dissenting opinion of Imam Zufar. We also cover a special rule for land lent for planting.

Guided Path
1
State the general rule for aariyah revocation
Identify that without a specified time, revoking incurs no guarantee. The lender may take back the item anytime.
This is the default position.
2
Identify the exception: time specified
When the lender fixes a known duration, the borrower relies on it. If the lender revokes early, he must compensate for the decrease in value caused by removal.
The text says 'ضمن ما نقص بالقلع'.
3
Present Zufar's objection
Zufar argues no guarantee because the borrower knew the lender retained the right to revoke and consented to that risk.
His proof: 'لما علم أن له ولاية الأخذ فقد رضي بذلك'.
4
Present the Hanafi response
The majority respond that specifying a time creates a reasonable expectation of fulfillment. Breaking it is deception (ghurur), so the lender must guarantee the loss. This differs from the case without a time.
The text says 'فقد غره بخلفه، فيضمن بخلاف غير الموقت'.
5
Apply the special rule for planted land
If land is lent for planting, the lender cannot take it back until harvest, whether a time was specified or not. This protects the growing crop.
Also note that the cost of returning the borrowed item (mu'unat al-radd) is on the borrower, and for wadi'ah on the depositor.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يضمن إن لم يُوقت، وإن وقت ورجع قبله ضمن ما نقص بالقلع، وقال زفر: لا ضمان عليه؛ لأنه لما علم أن له ولاية الأخذ فقد رضي بذلك، ولنا: أنه لما وقت وقتاً معلوماً، فالظاهر الوفاء بما وعد فقد اعتمد على قوله، ووثق به فقد غره بخلفه، فيضمن بخلاف غير الموقت. وإن أعارها ليزرعها لا تؤخذ حتى يحصد، وقت أو لم يوقت. ومؤونة الرد على المستعير والمودع.
And there is no guarantee if he did not specify a time. And if he did specify a time and revoked before it, he guarantees the deficiency caused by removal. Zufar said: no guarantee upon him, because when (the borrower) knew that he (the lender) has the authority to take, he consented to that. And our proof: when he specified a known time, the apparent is fulfillment of the promise; he (borrower) relied on his word and trusted him, so he deceived him by breaking it, thus he guarantees, unlike the unspecific case. And if he lent it for planting, it is not taken until harvest, whether time was specified or not. And the cost of return is upon the borrower and the depositor.
Source pages p. 124

Commentary
This passage covers three sub-rulings. First, if no time is fixed, revoking incurs no guarantee. Second, if a time is fixed and the lender revokes before that time, he must compensate for the decrease in value caused by removal. Imam Zufar dissents, arguing the borrower accepted the risk. The majority (including Abu Hanifa) hold that the borrower relied on the promise, so revocation is deceptive (gharar). Third, if land is lent for planting, the lender must wait until harvest, even if no time was specified; this protects the crop. Finally, the cost of returning the borrowed item is borne by the borrower (mu'unat al-radd), and for a deposit (wadi'ah), by the depositor.

Key Terms
التوقيت (al-tawqit): Specifying a time for the duration of aariyah
الضمان (al-daman): Liability to compensate for loss or damage
الغُرور (al-ghurur): Deception or misleading; the lender by promising a time deceives the borrower
مؤونة الرد (mu'unat al-radd): The cost of returning the borrowed item to the lender

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority Hanafi view, what is the ruling if the lender revokes before the specified time?
A) No guarantee because aariyah is non-binding
B) Lender guarantees the deficiency in value
C) Borrower must pay rent for the period used
D) The contract is void

Key Takeaway
In aariyah, specifying a time creates reliance; early revocation triggers guarantee for deficiency, except in Zufar's view.

Liability of Lender Upon Revocation of a Time-Bound Loan
Ruling on lender's liability for diminution when revoking a time-bound loan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on lender's liability when revoking a time-bound loan, identify Zufar's contrary view, and evaluate the basis for the majority position.

Core Idea
A lender who revokes a time-bound loan before the term ends must compensate for the resulting loss because the borrower relied on the promise.

You may think a lender can revoke a loan at any time without consequence. But what if a fixed period was agreed and the borrower acted in reliance? Hanafi jurists debated whether the lender must pay for the reduction in value of buildings or trees the borrower placed. This lesson unpacks that dispute and the argument from deception (taghrir).

Guided Path
1
State the Issue
Identify the exact legal question: When a lender revokes a time-bound loan before the term expires, is the lender liable for the diminution in value of any additions (buildings, trees) that the borrower must remove?
2
Identify the Majority Position
The majority (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) holds that the lender guarantees the diminution. Note the key condition: a set time and revocation before it.
This is the mufta bihi position.
3
Analyze Zufar's Opposition
Zufar argues no liability because the borrower knew the lender had the right to reclaim at any time, thus assumed the risk.
Zufar's view is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
4
Examine the Hanafi Response
The majority counter that setting a fixed term creates a reasonable expectation; the borrower relied on the promise, so revocation is a form of deception (taghrir) that triggers liability.
The dalil is aqli (rational), based on qiyas and istihsan.
5
Determine the Practical Consequence
In practice, under the majority view, the lender must pay the difference in value of the additions standing vs. removed, valued on the day of recall. Under Zufar's view, no compensation is owed.
The difference is a clear thamarah al-khilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يضمن إن لم يُوقت، وإن وقت ورجع قبله ضمن ما نقص بالقلع. ولا يضمن إلخ أي لا ضمان على المعير إذا رجع إن لم يوقت لها وقتا؛ لأنها غير لازمة ولم يغيره. [البحر الرائق: ٤٠٨/٧] وإن وقت إلخ أي وإن وقت المعير وقتاً معيناً، ورجع قبله أي قبل الوقت الذي عينه، ضمن ما نقص البناء أو الغرس بالقلع، وقال زفر: لا ضمان عليه؛ لأنه لما علم أن له ولاية الأخذ فقد رضي بذلك، ولنا: أنه لما وقت وقتاً معلوماً، فالظاهر الوفاء بما وعد فقد اعتمد على قوله، ووثق به فقد غره بخلفه، فيضمن بخلاف غير الموقت، والذي ذكره الشيخ في الضمان هو قول القدوري، وقيل: يضمن رب الأرض قيمة الغرس والبناء، ويكونان له، وقيل: إن كان في القلع ضرر بالأرض، فالخيار لرب الأرض. [رمز الحقائق: ٢٥٨/٢] ورجع قبله إلخ وهو أي الرجوع قبله مكروه؛ لأن فيه خلف الوعد، كذا في "الدرر"، وظاهره أنها تحريمية، لكن صرح القهستاني بأنها تنزيهية، ووفق شيخنا بحمل ما ذكره القهستاني على ما إذا وعد، وكان من نيته الوفاء، ثم طرء الخلف، فلا مخالفة. (فتح) ما نقص بالقلع: أي ضمن المعير ما نقص بالقلع بأن يقوم قائما غير مقلوع يعني بكم يشترى بشرط قيامه إلى المدة المضروبة، كذا في "النهاية"، وتعتبر القيمة يوم الاسترداد كما في "فتاوى قاضي خان". [البحر الرائق: ٤٠٨/٧]
And he is not liable if he did not set a time, but if he set a time and revoked before it, he is liable for the diminution caused by removal. 'And he is not liable etc.' means: no liability on the lender if he revokes without setting a time, because the loan is not binding and he did not change it. [Bahr al-Ra'iq 7:408] 'And if he set a time etc.' means: if the lender set a specific time and revoked before that time, he is liable for the diminution of the building or planting due to removal. Zufar said: there is no liability, because the borrower knew that the lender had the right to take it back, so he consented. Our evidence: when he set a known time, the apparent duty is to fulfill the promise, so the borrower relied on his word and trusted him, thus he deceived him by breaking his word, so he is liable, unlike the non-time-bound case. What the shaykh mentioned regarding liability is the statement of al-Quduri. And it is said: the landowner guarantees the value of the plants and buildings, and they become his. And it is said: if removal harms the land, the landowner has the choice. [Rasm al-Haqa'iq 2:258] 'And revoked before it etc.' means: revoking before the time is disliked (makruh) because it breaks a promise, as in al-Durar. Its apparent meaning is that it is prohibitively disliked, but al-Qahistani stated it is tanzihan, and our shaykh reconciled by interpreting al-Qahistani's statement as when he promised and intended to fulfill, then a situation arose, so no contradiction. (Fath) 'What is diminished by removal': meaning the lender guarantees the diminution by removal, such that it is valued standing, not uprooted, i.e., how much it would be bought with the condition of remaining until the set period, as in al-Nihayah. And the value is considered on the day of recall, as in Fatawa Qadi Khan. [Bahr al-Ra'iq 7:408]
Source pages p. 125

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute within the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq. It first states the ruling: if a lender revokes a loan without a fixed term, there is no liability. But if a term was set and the lender revokes before it ends, he guarantees the reduction in value of any building or trees that must be removed. The commentary explains that this liability arises because the borrower relied on the promise; the lender's breach is a form of deception (taghrir). Zufar disagreed, arguing that the borrower knew the lender could take it back, so there is no liability. The Hanafi response is that the set time created reliance. The text also mentions alternative opinions: some say the lender must pay the full value and keep the structures; others give the landowner an option if removal harms the land. The act of revoking before the time is considered makruh; there is a difference of opinion on whether it is makruh tahrimi or tanzihi, with the preferred view being tanzihi if the lender originally intended to honor the term. The measure of damages is the difference in value of the building/trees standing vs. removed, valued at the date of recall.

Key Terms
عارية (ariyah): A loan of a non-consumable item for use, without compensation.
معير (mu'ir): The lender who gives the item as a loan.
مستعير (musta'ir): The borrower who receives the item for use.
غرور (ghurur): Deception that induces reliance; here, the lender's breach of promise deceives the borrower.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the lender guarantee the diminution when revoking a time-bound loan according to the Hanafi school?
A) Because the loan contract is considered a sale
B) Because the borrower relied on the set time and the lender's breach is deception
C) Because the lender owns the buildings on the land
D) Because the borrower did not take proper care of the item

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a lender who revokes a time-bound loan before the term ends must compensate for any diminution caused, because the borrower relied on the promise.
