Death and Increase as Preventers of Gift Revocation
Explains that death of donor/donee and increase in value prevent revocation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two events that prevent a donor from revoking a gift in Hanafi fiqh and apply the qiyas that supports the ruling.

Core Idea
Gift revocation is blocked by death or increase – the donor's option is personal and does not survive.

In Hanafi fiqh, a donor generally has the right to revoke a gift, but that right is lost under certain conditions. This lesson examines two critical events – the death of either party and a physical increase in the gifted property – that permanently extinguish the revocation option. The passage uses qiyas (analogical reasoning) to demonstrate why these events are decisive.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two preventers
Read the passage and list the two events that block revocation: death of donor or donee, and physical increase that adds value.
The passage uses 'al-mim' for death and 'al-sin' for increase.
2
Understand the effect of donor's death
When the donor dies, his option to revoke becomes void. The passage analogizes it to the option of inspection (khiyar al-ru'ya) and option of condition (khiyar al-shart) – personal rights that are not inherited.
This is a qiyas: the option to revoke is a personal right (haqq shakhsi).
3
Understand the effect of donee's death
When the donee dies, ownership transfers to his heirs. The donor cannot revoke from them because they received ownership from the donee, not from the donor. This is analogized to a change of substance of the gift.
The passage says 'change of ownership is like change of the physical substance'.
4
Understand the effect of increase
A physical increase in the gifted object that raises its value makes the object effectively a different entity, preventing revocation. Even a slight increase suffices.
The increase must be in the body of the gift (e.g., growth, offspring), not merely a price rise.
5
Apply the qiyas framework
Summarize the analogy: the donor's right to revoke is like an option – it is a personal right that ends with death and cannot be transmitted. Similarly, increase transforms the gift, removing the original object.
This strengthens the Hanafi position that revocation is blocked in these cases.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والسمن: الزيادة ما في الجسم الموجبة لزيادة القيمة والميم موت إلخ أي الميم إشارة إلى موت أحد المتعاقدين: الواهب أو الموهوب له، فإذا مات الموهوب له أو الواهب يمنع الرجوع من الواهب ومن ورثة الواهب؛ لأن بموت الواهب يبطل خياره؛ لأنه وصف له، وهو لا يورث كخيار الرؤية والشرط، وبموت الموهوب له ينتقل الملك إلى ورثته، وهم لم يستفيدوا من جهة الواهب، فلا يرجع عليهم، كما إذا انتقل إليهم حال حياته، ولأن تبدل الملك كتبدل العين، فصار كعين أخرى.
And 'al-sin': the increase in the body that causes an increase in value, and 'al-mim': death etc. That is, 'al-mim' indicates the death of one of the two contracting parties: the donor or the donee. When the donee or the donor dies, it prevents revocation by the donor and by the donor's heirs; because with the donor's death his option becomes void, as it is a personal right and is not inherited like the option of inspection and the option of condition. And with the donee's death, ownership transfers to his heirs, and they did not receive benefit from the donor's side, so he cannot revoke against them, just as if ownership had transferred to them during his lifetime. And because change of ownership is like change of the physical substance, so it becomes like another substance.
Source pages p. 134

Commentary
This passage explains two factors that prevent the revocation of a gift: increase in the gifted property's value and the death of either party. The increase is a physical increase in the body of the gift that raises its value; if the donee adds such an increase, the donor loses the right to revoke. Death of either the donor or the donee also blocks revocation. If the donor dies, his right to revoke dies with him because it is a non-inheritable option. If the donee dies, the gift becomes the property of his heirs, and the donor cannot reclaim it from them because the ownership changed hands similarly to a transfer during life. The reasoning uses qiyas: change of ownership is analogized to change of the physical substance of the gift, making it a different entity.

Key Terms
الرجوع في الهبة (al-ruju' fi al-hiba): The donor's right to take back a gift after it has been given and accepted.
الموت (al-mawt): Death of donor or donee, which in this context prevents revocation.
الزيادة (al-ziyada): Physical increase in the gifted object that adds value, such as growth or offspring.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the donor's death prevent his heirs from revoking a gift he made?
A) Because the heirs are not the original donor
B) Because the right to revoke is a personal option that does not inherit
C) Because the gift already left his ownership
D) Because the donee has already taken possession

Key Takeaway
Death of donor or donee, or a physical increase in the gifted property, permanently blocks the donor's right to revoke a gift.

Explicit Declaration of Compensation in Gifts
Ruling that compensation must be explicitly stated to waive revocation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition for a donee's payment to extinguish the donor's right to revoke a gift and distinguish it from an independent gift.

Core Idea
To extinguish the right to revoke, compensation must be explicitly declared as such.

In Hanafi law, a gift (hiba) is revocable by the donor unless the donee gives compensation (ʿiwad). However, not just any payment suffices—the compensation must be explicitly designated as the price for the gift. Without that declaration, the payment is treated as a separate independent gift, leaving both parties free to revoke. This lesson unpacks the ruling and its practical implications.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling on revocation
Begin with the default rule: a donor may revoke a gift unless compensation is given and accepted. Identify the legal effect of proper compensation: the right of revocation is permanently extinguished.
The right of revocation is a right of the donor, so only his satisfaction with compensation can waive it.
2
Identify the condition for valid compensation
The donee must explicitly state that what he gives is compensation for the gift. The text gives formulas: 'Take this as compensation for your gift, or its substitute, or in exchange for it.' Without such wording, the payment is not considered ʿiwad.
The explicit declaration is necessary because the donor's right is established and cannot be waived by implication.
3
Apply the condition to a case
Suppose the donee gives the donor a sum of money without saying it is for the gift. According to the text, this is a new independent gift (hiba mubtadaʿa), and each party may revoke their own gift.
If the donee later claims it was intended as compensation, it has no legal effect without prior declaration.
4
Analyze the third-party scenario
If a stranger volunteers compensation and the donor accepts, the revocation right is also extinguished. However, the volunteer cannot claim reimbursement from the donee unless the donee expressly guaranteed it.
This reinforces the principle that the compensation must be intended by the donor to waive his right, and the volunteer's intention alone does not create a debt on the donee.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والعين العوض: يعني أن المراد من العين العوض، وفسره بقوله : فإن "قال" أي الموهوب له للواهب: "خذه" أي هذا الشيء "عوض هبتك أو بدلها أو بمقابلتها، فقبضه الواهب سقط الرجوع" لما روينا، ولابد من ذكر الموهوب له أن المدفوع عوض عن الهبة، وقد أشار الشيخ إليه بقوله : خذه عوض هبتك أو بدلها أو بمقابلتها"؛ لأن حق الرجوع ثابت له ولا يسقط الرجوع إلا بعوض يرضى به هو، ويشترط فيه شرائط الهبة من القبض والإفراز، ولو وهب للواهب شيئا، ولم يذكره أنه عوض عنها كان هبة مبتدأة فلكل واحد منهما أن يرجع في هبته. رمز الحقائق: ٢٦٤/٢] وصح إلخ: أي إن عوضه أجنبي عن الموهوب له ومتبرعا، فقبض الواهب العوض، بطل حق الرجوع، ثم المتبرع لا يرجع على الموهوب له بما عوضه وإن أمره به ما لم يضمن الموهوب له صريحا.
And 'al-ayn' is the compensation: meaning that what is meant by 'al-ayn' is the compensation. He explains it by saying: 'For he said'—i.e., the donee to the donor—'Take this thing as compensation for your gift, or its substitute, or in exchange for it.' Then the donor took possession of it, the right of revocation falls. This is based on what we narrated. It is necessary that the donee mention that what is given is compensation for the gift, as the teacher (the author) indicated by his saying: 'Take it as compensation for your gift, or its substitute, or in exchange for it.' Because the right of revocation is established for him, and revocation does not fall except with a compensation that he is satisfied with. The conditions of a gift—possession and segregation—are required in it. If the donee gave something to the donor and did not mention that it was compensation for it, it is an independent gift, and each of them may revoke his gift. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2:264) 'And it is valid etc.': i.e., if a third party, unrelated to the donee and voluntarily, gives compensation, and the donor takes possession of it, the right of revocation becomes void. Then the volunteer does not have recourse against the donee for what he compensated, even if the donee ordered him to do so, unless the donee explicitly guaranteed it.
Source pages p. 134

Commentary
This passage clarifies the rule that compensation ('iwad) given by the donee to the donor must be explicitly stated as compensation for the gift in order to extinguish the donor's right to revoke. The donor says something like 'Take this as compensation for your gift' or 'in exchange for it.' If done, and the donor takes possession, the right of revocation is lost forever. Without such explicit mention, the transaction is treated as a new independent gift (hiba mubtada'a), allowing both parties to revoke their respective gifts. This requirement exists because the donor's right of revocation is a right of the donor; it can only be extinguished by compensation that he agrees to. Furthermore, if a third party voluntarily provides compensation, the donor's revocation right is voided, but that third party cannot claim reimbursement from the donee unless the donee expressly guaranteed it. The conditions of a valid gift—delivery and segregation—also apply to the compensation itself.

Key Terms
العوض (al-'iwad): Something given in exchange for the gift to prevent the donor from revoking.
هبة مبتدأة (hiba mubtada'a): An independent gift not connected to the previous gift.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Yes, because the money is an independent gift
B) No, because the donor accepted the money
C) Yes, but only if the money is less than the gift's value
D) No, because any payment waives revocation

Key Takeaway
Compensation must be explicitly declared as such to waive the donor's right of revocation; otherwise, it is a separate gift with no effect on the original.

Partial Recovery of Gift or Compensation
Intra-Hanafi dispute on partial recovery of compensation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rules for partial recovery of the gift or compensation in hibah transactions and distinguish between the relied-upon position and that of Imam Zufar.

Core Idea
Partial loss of gift or compensation triggers proportional adjustment, not automatic voidance.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq and its commentary presents three scenarios involving partial recovery of either the gifted property or the compensation given for it. The central question is: when a third party reclaims part of the property, how does this affect the rights of donor and donee? The relied-upon Hanafi position requires the donor to return any remaining compensation before revoking, while Imam Zufar allows immediate revocation. Understanding this ikhtilaf is essential for correctly adjudicating hibah disputes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three scenarios
The passage presents three distinct cases: (a) half of the gifted property is reclaimed by a third party; (b) half of the compensation given by the donee is reclaimed; (c) the donee compensates only half of the gift's value.
Each case has a different ruling regarding the rights of donor and donee.
2
Extract the ruling for each scenario
For scenario (a): the donee recovers half the compensation from the donor. For (b): the donor cannot revoke until the remaining compensation is returned. For (c): the donor may revoke the uncompensated half.
Scenario (b) is the focus of the intra-Hanafi dispute.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute
Imam Zufar holds that in scenario (b) the donor may revoke immediately, even without returning the remaining compensation. The majority (Abu Hanifa and Sahibayn) require the return of the remaining compensation first.
The majority's reasoning: compensation was given for the whole gift, so partial loss requires restoration.
4
Apply the relied-upon position
Use the principle that the compensation is a counterpart to the entire gift. Thus, if part of the compensation is lost, the donor must restore the remaining portion before revocation.
The mufta bihi is the majority view.
5
Evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: a donor following Zufar could revoke immediately, while one following the majority must return the remaining compensation first.
In fatwa, the mufti follows the majority.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن استحق إلخ أي وإن استحق نصف الهبة رجع الموهوب له على الواهب بنصف العوض؛ لأنه لم يدفع إليه إلا أن يسلم الموهوب له كله، فإذا فات بعضه رجع عليه بقدره. [رمز الحقائق: ٢٦٤/٢] وبعكسه لا: أي إن استحق نصف العوض لا يرجع الواهب في الهبة بشيء حتى يرد الواهب ما بقي من العوض، فحينئذ يرجع بها، وقال زفر محله: إذا استحق نصف العوض، له أن يرجع في الهبة وإن كان لا يقبل القسمة. (مسكين ولو عوض النصف أي ولو عوض الموهوب له نصف الهبة رجع الواهب بما لم يعوض، وهو النصف الباقي؛ لأن حقه في الرجوع كان في الكل، فإذا عوضه عن بعضه امتنع الرجوع في حصته، وبقي في الباقي على ما كان رمز الحقائق: ٢٦٤/٢] رجع بما لم يعوض: لأن المانع قد خص النصف، غاية ما فيه أنه يلزم منه الشيوع في الهبة، لكنه طارئ، فلا يضره كما قدمنا [البحر الرائق: ٤٢٥/٧]
And 'if half is reclaimed etc.' i.e., if half of the gift is reclaimed (by a third party), the donee recovers from the donor half of the compensation; because he (the donee) only gave it on condition that the entire gift would be delivered; when some part is lost, he recovers proportionally. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2:264] And its reverse is not: i.e., if half of the compensation is reclaimed, the donor does not revoke the gift at all until he returns the remaining compensation; then he may revoke. Zufar says in its place: when half of the compensation is reclaimed, he may revoke the gift even if it is indivisible. (Mulla Miskin) 'And if he compensates half' i.e., if the donee compensates half of the gift, the donor revokes what was not compensated, which is the remaining half; because his right of revocation was in the whole; when he compensates for part, revocation is prevented in that portion, and remains in the remainder as before. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2:264] He revokes what was not compensated, because the obstacle (compensation) is specific to that half; at most this leads to co-ownership in the gift, but it is incidental, so it does not harm, as we previously stated. [Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 7:425]
Source pages p. 134

Commentary
This passage addresses three scenarios of partial recovery. First, if half of the gifted property is reclaimed (e.g., a third party proves ownership), then the donee can recover half of the compensation he gave to the donor, because he gave the compensation in expectation of full ownership. Second, the reverse: if half of the compensation is reclaimed (e.g., a third party proves ownership of the compensation item), the donor cannot revoke the gift at all unless he first returns the remaining compensation to the donee. Imam Zufar disagrees and says the donor can revoke immediately even if the remaining compensation cannot be divided. Third, if the donee compensates only half of the gift (e.g., gives cash equal to half its value), the donor may revoke the other half, because his full right to revoke is only partially extinguished by the partial compensation. This may create co-ownership in the gift, but that is acceptable as an incidental result.

Key Terms
استحقاق (istihqaq): Reclamation of property by a rightful owner, voiding the donor's title.
شيوع (shuyu'): Co-ownership of the gifted property between donor and donee.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a third party reclaims half of the compensation the donee gave, according to the relied-upon Hanafi position, what must the donor do before revoking the gift?
A) Return the entire compensation to the donee
B) Return the remaining half of the compensation
C) Nothing; he can revoke immediately
D) Wait for the donee to return the gift

Key Takeaway
In hibah, partial recovery of the gift or compensation results in proportional adjustment, and the donor cannot revoke the gift unless the remaining compensation is returned (according to the relied-upon position).

Gift Leaving Donee's Ownership Prevents Revocation
Ruling that if the donee resells or regifts, the donor cannot revoke

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a donor loses the right to revoke a gift and apply the partial revocation rule when the donee sells or disposes of part of the gifted property.

Core Idea
Once the gift leaves the donee's ownership, the donor's right to revoke is extinguished.

This lesson examines the first of three factors that prevent a donor from revoking a gift: the gift leaving the donee's ownership (khuruj al-hiba). The source text from Kanz al-Daqa'iq and its commentary by Mulla Miskin explain that if the donee sells, gifts, or consumes the gifted item (or part of it), the donor's right to revoke is either entirely or partially lost. We will unpack the ruling, its underlying rationale based on the donor's implied permission, and the evidence from the hadith of Barirah. Understanding this principle is essential for correctly determining when a donor can take back a gift.

Guided Path
1
State the base ruling
When the donee transfers the gift to a third party by sale, gift, or consumption, the donor's right to revoke is lost.
2
Explain the rationale
The donor empowered the donee by giving the gift; hence the donor cannot object to the donee's disposal. The new ownership is a fresh cause, like the renewal of the physical substance.
Based on the commentary's reference to the hadith of Barirah.
3
Analyze the partial disposal case
If the donee sells only half of the gift, the donor may revoke the unsold half. The obstacle (prevention) only applies to the extent of the disposal.
The text says: 'وببيع نصفها رجع في النصف كعدم بيع شيء'.
4
Examine the dalil
The story of Barirah illustrates that when ownership changes, the original owner's right is extinguished, analogized to the renewal of the object itself.
The hadith: The Prophet (SAW) allowed Aisha to give Barirah as a gift, and when Barirah was later freed, her former master could not claim her.
5
Apply to consumption and onward gifts
If the gift is consumed (e.g., money borrowed and spent), the donor cannot revoke because it has left the donee's ownership. If the donee regifts it and the second donee returns it to the donor, the original donor may revoke only after the second donee returns it.
From the commentary's reference to Fatawa Qadikhan and al-Mabsut.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والخاء خروج الهبة من ملك الموهوب له، وببيع نصفها رجع في النصف كعدم بيع شيء، والزاء الزوجية، فلو وهب ثم نكحها رجع، وبالعكس لا، والقاف القرابة، فلو وهب لذي رحم محرم منه لا يرجع. والخاء خروج الهبة إلخ [ بأن باع الهبة أو وهب لآخر أي حرف الخاء إشارة إلى ذلك؛ لأنه حصل بتسليط الواهب، فلا ينقضه، ولأنه تجدد الملك بتجدد سببه، وهو كتجدد العين بدليل قصة بريرة ما، وأطلق في الخروج، فشمل ما إذا وهب لإنسان دراهم، ثم استقرضها منه فإنه لا يرجع فيها لاستهلاكها، كذا في "فتاوى قاضي خان"، وشمل أيضا ما إذا وهبها الموهوب له، فإنه لا رجوع للواهب الأول إلا إذا رجع الثاني، فللواهب الأول حينئذ الرجوع سواء كان بقبض أو تراض كذا في "المبسوط". [البحر الرائق: ٤٢٥/٧] وببيع نصفها إلخ أي وهب دارا وقبضها الموهوب له ثم باع نصفها فللواهب أن . يرجع في النصف كعدم بيع شيء أي إن لم . شيئا منها، له أن يبع يرجع في نصفها، قال في "البحر": لأن المانع وجد في البعض، فيمتنع بقدره كما كان له أن النصف، والعين كلها لم تخرج عن ملك الموهوب له؛ لأن له حق الرجوع في الكل، فله أن يستوفيه أو بعضه البحر الرائق: ٤٢٥/٧] (ملا مسكين)
And 'al-kha' is the exit of the gift from the ownership of the donee, and by selling half of it, he revokes in half, like not selling anything. And 'al-zay' is marital relationship, so if he (donor) gave a gift and then married her, he may revoke; and the opposite not. And 'al-qaf' is kinship, so if he gave to a mahram relative by blood, he cannot revoke. 'And al-kha' exit of the gift etc.' [i.e., by selling the gift or giving it as a gift to another. The letter 'kha' indicates that; because it occurred with the donor's empowerment, so he cannot nullify it. And because ownership is renewed by a new cause, like the renewal of the physical substance, as evidenced by the story of Barirah. And he (the author) made exit general, so it includes if someone gave another dirhams, then borrowed them back from him—he does not revoke because they are consumed. This is in Fatawa Qadikhan. And it also includes if the donee gives it away as a gift; then the first donor cannot revoke unless the second (donee) returns it; then the first donor may revoke, whether by delivery or mutual consent, as in al-Mabsut. [Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 7:425] 'And by selling half of it etc.' i.e., if someone gave a house and the donee took possession, then he sold half of it, the donor may revoke that half, as if nothing was sold. Because the obstacle (revocation prevention) only applies to part; so it is prevented to that extent, just as he had the right to revoke half. And the whole substance did not leave the donee's ownership, because the donor has a right to revoke the whole, so he may take the whole or part of it. [Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 7:425] (Mulla Miskin)
Source pages p. 134

Commentary
This passage introduces a set of three letters (kh, z, q) each indicating a factor that prevents revocation. The first is 'kh' meaning exit of the gift from the donee's ownership. If the donee sells the gift or gives it to another as a gift, the original donor loses the right to revoke. The rationale is that the donee's disposal was made possible by the donor's original gift, and the new ownership is a fresh cause. The text references the story of Barirah as an analogy. However, if the donee sells only half of the gift, the donor can revoke that half, because the right to revoke attaches to the portion still owned. The ruling covers cases of consumption (e.g., borrowing and spending money) and even gifts onward: if the donee gives it away, the first donor cannot revoke unless the second donee returns it. Then the first donor may revoke. The passage then transitions to marriage (z) and kinship (q), which are covered in the next lesson.

Key Terms
خروج الهبة (khuruj al-hiba): The gifted property leaving the donee's ownership by sale, gift, or consumption.
تسليط الواهب (taslit al-wahib): The donor's implicit permission for the donee to dispose of the gift.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A donee sells half of the gifted house. What can the donor do?
A) Revoke the entire house
B) Revoke only the unsold half
C) Cannot revoke any part because the house was in the donee's possession
D) Must wait until the donee repurchases the half

Key Takeaway
If the donee transfers ownership of the gift, the donor's right to revoke is lost, except that partial transfer allows partial revocation.

intermediate
12 min
Prevention of Revocation of Gift: Causes and Proofs
Commentary on the mnemonics for prevention of revocation of gift

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four causes that prevent revocation of a gift and state the Hanafi ruling and evidence for each.

Core Idea
Revocation of a gift is prevented when the donee disposes of it, marries the donor, is a mahram relative, or when the gift is destroyed.

In Hanafi law, a donor generally has the right to revoke a gift and take back the gifted object. However, certain situations arise where this right is suspended or permanently lost. This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq, through its famous mnemonic 'خ ز ق ه', explains the four causes that prevent revocation. Understanding these causes is essential for correctly applying the rules of gift in daily transactions.

Guided Path
1
Understand the general permissibility of revocation
In Hanafi fiqh, a donor may revoke a gift after it has been given and possessed, unless a preventing cause exists. This is the baseline rule.
This is different from Shafi'i, where revocation is generally not allowed.
2
Identify the mnemonic letters
The matn uses four letters: خ (khā'), ز (zā'), ق (qāf), and ه (hā'). Each stands for a cause preventing revocation.
These letters are clues to the causes: exit from ownership, marriage, kinship, and destruction.
3
Analyze the cause of disposal (خ)
If the donee sells, gives away, or otherwise disposes of the gifted object (or part of it), the donor cannot revoke that part. The donee's action is valid because the donor permitted ownership.
If the donee only disposes of part, the donor can revoke the remaining part.
4
Analyze marriage and kinship causes (ز and ق)
If the donor and donee are married at the time of the gift, or if the donee is a mahram relative by blood, revocation is prevented. For marriage, the crucial moment is the gift time, not the revocation time.
For kinship, only mahram by blood (not by fosterage or marriage) prevents revocation.
5
Examine destruction and method of revocation (ه and conclusion)
If the gifted object is destroyed, revocation is impossible. The donee is believed if he claims destruction. Revocation can only occur by mutual consent or a judicial ruling; unilateral revocation is ineffective.
Until one of these occurs, the donee remains owner and can dispose of the object.

Source Text

الرجوع في الهبة
والخاء خروج الهبة من ملك الموهوب له، وببيع نصفها رجع في النصف كعدم بيع شيء، والزاء الزوجية، فلو وهب ثم نكحها رجع، وبالعكس لا، والقاف القرابة، فلو وهب لذي رحم محرم لا يرجع. والخاء خروج الهبة إلخ [ بأن باع الهبة أو وهب لآخر أي حرف الخاء إشارة إلى ذلك؛ لأنه حصل بتسليط الواهب، فلا ينقضه، ولأنه تجدد الملك بتجدد سببه، وهو كتجدد العين بدليل قصة بريرة ما، وأطلق في الخروج، فشمل ما إذا وهب لإنسان دراهم، ثم استقرضها منه فإنه لا يرجع فيها لاستهلاكها، كذا في "فتاوى قاضي خان"، وشمل أيضا ما إذا وهبها الموهوب له، فإنه لا رجوع للواهب الأول إلا إذا رجع الثاني، فللواهب الأول حينئذ الرجوع سواء كان بقبض أو تراض كذا في "المبسوط". [البحر الرائق: ٤٢٥/٧] وببيع نصفها إلخ أي وهب دارا وقبضها الموهوب له ثم باع نصفها فللواهب أن يرجع في النصف كعدم بيع شيء أي إن لم يبع شيئا منها، له أن يرجع في نصفها، قال في "البحر": لأن المانع وجد في البعض، فيمتنع بقدره كما كان له أن يرجع في النصف، والعين كلها لم تخرج عن ملك الموهوب له؛ لأن له حق الرجوع في الكل، فله أن يستوفيه أو بعضه البحر الرائق: ٤٢٥/٧] (ملا مسكين)
والزاء الزوجية أي الزوجية مانعة من الرجوع وقت الهبة لا وقت الرجوع؛ لأنها نظير القرابة في التواصل بدليل جريان التوارث بينهما، فكان المقصود الصلة وقد حصل. (درر) وفي فتاوى قاضي خان" من المهر: بعث إلى امرأته متاعا، بعثت أيضا، ثم افترقا بعد الزفاف، وادعى أنه عارية، وأراد الاسترداد، وأرادت الاسترداد أيضا، يسترد كل ما أعطى؛ لأن المرأة زعمت أن الإعطاء كان عوضا عن الهبة و لم تثبت الهبة، فلا يثبت العوض إلخ، وفي "فتاوى قاضي خان": ولو وهبت المرأة شيئا لزوجها، وادعت أنه استكرهها في الهبة تسمع دعواها. [البحر الرائق: ٤٢٦/٧] فلو وهب إلخ: أي لو وهب رجل لأجنبية ثم نكح رجع؛ لأن المعتبر حالة الهبة، فإن كانت أجنبية فيها كان مقصوده العوض فيثبت الرجوع فيها، فلا يسقط بالتزوج، وإن كانت حليلة كان مقصوده الصلة دون العوض، وقد حصل، فسقط الرجوع، فلا يعود بالإبانة كذا في الزيلعي (فتح) وبالعكس لا: أي عكس الحكم المذكور بأن وهب لزوجته ثم أبالها، لا يرجع؛ لأن المقصود فيها الصلة كما في القرابة. [رمز الحقائق: ٢٦٤/٢] والقاف القرابة [المحرمية بالرحم لا بالمصاهرة] لأن المقصود منها صلة الرحم، وقد حصل، وفي الرجوع قطيعة الرحم، فلا يرجع سواء كان مسلما أو كافرا. [رمز الحقائق: ٢٦٤/٢]

كتاب الهبة
۱۳۵
الرجوع في الهبة
لا يرجع فيها، والهاء الهلاك، فلو ادعاه صدق، وإنما يصح الرجوع عن الهبة
لا يرجع إلخ لحديث الحاكم مرفوعا : إذا كانت الهبة لذي رحم محرم لم يرجع فيها"، وصححه، وقال: على شرط الشيخين ومفهوم شرطه أنها إذا كانت لغير محرم فله الرجوع، فهو حجة على الشافعي له؛ لأنه قائل بالمفاهيم وأئمتنا وإن لم يعتبروه لكن صرح به في أثر ابن عمر لهما على ما رواه عبد الرزاق في "مصنفه" "من وهب هبة لغير ذي رحم، فله أن يرجع فيها إلا أن يثاب منها"، خرجه الحافظ الزيلعي، ولأنه قد حصل مقصوده، وهو صلة الرحم، أطلقه، فشمل المحرم المسلم والذمي والمستأمن كذا في "المبسوط". وقيد بالرحم؛ لأن المحرم كأخيه الرضاعة وأمهات النساء والربائب وأزواج البنين والبنات لا يمنع الرجوع. وقيد بالمحرم؛ لأن الرحم بلا محرم كابن عمه لا يمنع الرجوع، وفي ذكر القرابة ثم تفسيرها بالرحم المحرم إشارة إلى أنه لو وهب لرحم محرم لا من جهة القرابة كان له الرجوع كما لو وهب لابن عمه، وهو أخوه رضاعاً، وخرج ما لو وهب لعبد أخيه أو لأخيه وهو عبد لأجنبي، فإنه يرجع فيها عند أبي حنيفة؛ لأن الملك لم يقع فيها للقريب من كل وجه بدليل أن العبد أحق بما وهب إليه إذا احتاج إليه وقالا : لا يرجع في الأولى، ويرجع في الثانية، محرم من الواهب، فلا رجوع فيها اتفاقاً على الأصح؛ لأن الهبة لأيهما وقعت تمنع الرجوع رحم كذا في "المبسوط". [البحر الرائق: ٤٢٦/٧] والهاء الهلاك يعني هلاك العين الموهوبة مانع، وأما هلاك أحد العاقدين، فقد قدمه لتعذر الرجوع بعد الهلاك. [البحر الرائق: ٤٢٧/٧]
ولو كان ذا
فلو ادعاه صدق: أي لو ادعى الموهوب له هلاك الموهوب يصدق؛ لأنه منكر لوجوب الرد عليه، قيد بدعوى الهلاك؛ لأن الموهوب له لو ادعى أنه أخوه وأنكره الواهب يستحلف الواهب عند الكل؛ لأنه ادعى بسبب النسب مالا لازما، فكان المقصود إثباته دون النسب، ذكره قاضي خان في "فتاواه" من "باب" الاستحلاف"، وأشار بقوله: "صدق" إلى أن القول قوله بغير يمين ولهذا قال في "الخلاصة": لو قال الموهوب له هلكت، فالقول قوله، ولا يمين عليه، فإن قال الواهب هي هذه حلف المنكر أنها ليست هذه إلخ. [البحر الرائق: ٤٢٧/٧] وإنما يصح الرجوع إلخ: أي وإنما يصح الرجوع عن الهبة بأحد الأمرين: إما بتراضيهما أي الواهب والموهوب له، أو بحكم الحاكم بالرجوع؛ لأن حكم العقد قد ثبت وتم والرفع بعد الثبوت يتوقف على فسخ من له ولاية الفسخ، وهو القاضي والمتعاقدان كالرد بالعيب بعد القبض، فما لم يقض القاضي أو لم يفسخاها بالتراضي، فملك الموهوب له ثابت في العين حتى ينفذ تصرفه فيه من عتق وبيع وغير ذلك ولو كان بعد المرافعة إلى الحاكم، وكذا لو منعه، وهلك في يده لا يضمن؛ لقيام ملكه فيه وكذا لو هلك بعد القضاء قبل المنع، وإن منعه بعد القضاء ضمن؛ لوجود التعدي، وبكل منهما أي بالرضاء وبالقضاء يكون فسخا من الأصل، وعند زفر الله: الرجوع بالتراضي عقد جديد، فجعل بمنزلة الهبة المبتدأة، فكان للموهوب له الرجوع. [رمز الحقائق: ٢٦٥/٢]
Book of Gift. 134. Revocation of Gift. The letter khā' (خ) indicates the exit of the gift from the ownership of the donee. And by selling half of it, he revokes the half just as if he sold nothing. The letter zā' (ز) indicates marriage. So if someone gives a gift and then marries her, he revokes; but the reverse, no. The letter qāf (ق) indicates kinship. So if someone gives a gift to a mahram relative by blood, he does not revoke. The khā' (خ) for exiting the gift, etc. [If he sells the gift or gifts it to another, the letter khā' (خ) indicates that; because it occurred by the permission of the donor, so it is not invalidated by him, and because ownership is renewed by renewal of its cause, which is like the renewal of the substance as evidenced by the story of Barīrah. The wording for exit is general, so it includes if someone gives a gift of dirhams to a person, then borrows them from him, for he cannot revoke because they are consumed. This is from Fatawa Qadi Khan. It also includes if the donee gives it as a gift, then the first donor cannot revoke unless the second returns it, then the first donor can revoke whether it was with possession or mutual consent. This is from al-Mabsut. [al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 7/425] And selling half of it, etc.: i.e., someone gave a house and the donee took possession, then sold half of it. The donor may revoke half, just as if he sold nothing, i.e., if he did not sell anything, he can revoke half. He said in al-Bahr: because the impediment occurs in part, so it prevents to that extent, just as he could revoke half. And the entire asset has not left the ownership of the donee because the donor has the right to revoke the whole, so he may take it or part of it. [al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 7/425] (Mulla Miskeen) And the letter zā' (ز) for marriage: marriage prevents revocation at the time of the gift, not at the time of revocation. Because it is analogous to kinship in connection, evidenced by the inheritance between them. So the purpose was connection and it has been achieved. (Durar) And in Fatawa Qadi Khan regarding the dower: A man sent goods to his wife, she also sent something, then they separated after the wedding, and he claimed it was a loan and wanted to reclaim, and she also wanted to reclaim. Each reclaims what he gave, because the woman claimed that the giving was compensation for a gift, and the gift was not proven, so the compensation is not proven, etc. And in Fatawa Qadi Khan: If a woman gives a gift to her husband and claims he coerced her, her claim is heard. [al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 7/426] So if he gives a gift, etc.: i.e., if a man gives a gift to a woman not his wife and then marries her, he may revoke; because the consideration is at the time of the gift. If she was a stranger then, his intention was compensation, so revocation is established and is not nullified by marriage. If she was his wife, his intention was connection without compensation, and it has been achieved, so revocation is dropped, and it does not return by divorce. This is from al-Zayla'i (Fath). And the reverse, no: i.e., the opposite of the mentioned ruling: if he gave a gift to his wife and then divorced her, he does not revoke; because the purpose there is connection, like kinship. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2/264] And the letter qāf (ق) for kinship [mahram by blood, not by marriage] because the purpose is maintaining ties of kinship, and that has been achieved. And revocation would be severing ties, so he does not revoke, whether the recipient is Muslim or non-Muslim. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2/264] Page 136 Book of Gift 135 Revocation of Gift: He does not revoke it. And the letter hā' (ه) indicates destruction. If he claims it, he is believed. And revocation of the gift is only valid... He does not revoke based on the hadith of al-Hakim marfu': 'If the gift is to a mahram relative, he does not revoke it.' He authenticated it and said it is on the condition of the two shaykhs. Its conditional implication is that if it is to a non-mahram, then he may revoke; so it is an argument against al-Shafi'i because he holds that implications are valid. Our imams, although they do not consider it valid, it is explicitly stated in the athar of Ibn 'Umar from 'Abd al-Razzaq in his Musannaf: 'Whoever gives a gift to a non-relative, he may revoke it unless he receives compensation for it.' This was extracted by al-Hafiz al-Zayla'i. And because his purpose has been achieved, which is maintaining ties of kinship. It is general so it includes the mahram Muslim, dhimmi, and musta'min. This is from al-Mabsut. It is restricted to blood (rahm) because mahram like a brother through breastfeeding, mothers of women, step-daughters, wives' sons, and daughters do not prevent revocation. And it is restricted to mahram because a blood relative who is not mahram, like a cousin, does not prevent revocation. In mentioning kinship and then interpreting it as mahram by blood, there is an indication that if someone gives a gift to a mahram relative not through kinship (e.g., rada'ah), he may revoke, as if he gave to his cousin who is his foster brother. And excluded is if he gives to a slave of his brother, or to his brother who is a slave of a stranger; then Abu Hanifa says he revokes because ownership does not fully vest in the relative, evidenced by the fact that the slave is more entitled to what is given to him if he needs it. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say: He does not revoke in the first case, and revokes in the second. Mahram from the donor: then no revocation by agreement, on the correct view, because whichever of them the gift was made to prevents revocation due to kinship. This is in al-Mabsut. [al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 7/426] And the letter hā' (ه) for destruction means destruction of the gifted object prevents revocation. As for destruction of one of the contracting parties, it has been mentioned earlier due to impossibility of revocation after death. [al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 7/427] If he claims it, he is believed: i.e., if the donee claims the gifted object is destroyed, he is believed because he denies the obligation of returning it. It is restricted to the claim of destruction because if the donee claims that the donor is his brother and the donor denies, the donor is made to take an oath according to all, because he claimed a permanent right due to lineage. So the purpose is to prove the right, not lineage. This is mentioned by Qadi Khan in his Fatawa from the chapter of istihlaf. And by his saying 'he is believed', it indicates that the statement is accepted without oath. For this reason it is said in al-Khulasa: If the donee says 'it is destroyed', his statement is accepted and no oath is upon him. If the donor says 'this is it', the denier (donor) takes an oath that this is not the same, etc. [al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 7/427] And revocation is only valid by one of two means: either by mutual consent of the two, i.e., the donor and the donee, or by a ruling of the judge for revocation, because the ruling of the contract has been established and perfected, and its removal after establishment depends on annulment by one who has authority to annul, which is the judge and the two contracting parties, like returning due to defect after possession. So unless the judge rules or they annul it by mutual consent, the ownership of the donee remains in the object so that his disposal of it by manumission, sale, etc. is effective, even if after referral to the judge. Likewise, if the donor prevents him and it is destroyed in his hand, he is not liable because his ownership stands. And if it is destroyed after the ruling but before prevention, he is not liable. If he prevents after the ruling, he is liable because of transgression. By each means (mutual consent and judicial ruling), it is an annulment ab initio. According to Zufar: Revocation by mutual consent is a new contract, so it is like a new gift, and thus the donee has the right to revoke. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2/265]
Source pages p. 135

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the rules of revocation of gift (رجوع في الهبة) from the Hanafi madhhab. It explains the mnemonics 'خ ز ق ه' from the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq. The commentary proceeds by explaining each letter as a cause preventing revocation.

**Letter خ (خروج الهبة من ملك الموهوب له):** The first cause that prevents revocation is the exit of the gifted object from the donee's ownership by the donee's own action, such as selling or giving it to another. Once the object leaves the donee's ownership through his own disposal (which is valid by the donor's permission), the donor cannot revoke. This includes cases where the donee uses the object (e.g., borrows and consumes dirhams) or gives it to a third party. However, if the second donee returns the object, the first donor's right to revoke revives. If only half of the object is sold, the donor can revoke the remaining half because the impediment exists only in part.

**Letter ز (الزوجية):** Marriage between the donor and donee at the time of the gift is a cause preventing revocation. If a man gives a gift to a woman who is not his wife and later marries her, he can still revoke because the intention at the time of gift was compensation (عوض). Conversely, if he gives to his wife and later divorces her, he cannot revoke because the intention was connection (صلة), which has been achieved through marriage. The principle: The decisive factor is the relationship at the time of the gift, not at the time of revocation.

**Letter ق (القرابة):** The third cause is close blood kinship (رحم محرم). A gift to a mahram relative (by blood, not marriage or fosterage) prevents revocation because the purpose is maintaining ties of kinship. This applies to all mahram relatives, whether Muslim or non-Muslim. The key is that the kinship must be mahram and blood-based. If the relative is not mahram (e.g., a cousin) or mahram through other means (e.g., rada'ah), revocation is not prevented. There is a notable intra-madhhab dispute: If the donee is the slave of a relative, Abu Hanifa says the donor can revoke because ownership does not fully vest in the relative; the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) distinguish between giving to the slave of the relative (no revocation) and giving to the relative who is a slave of a stranger (revocation allowed).

**Letter ه (الهلاك):** The fourth cause is the destruction of the gifted object. If the donee claims it is destroyed, he is believed without oath because he is denying the obligation to return. Destruction of one of the parties (death) also prevents revocation due to impossibility.

**Manner of Revocation:** The passage concludes that revocation of a gift is valid only in two ways: (1) mutual consent of donor and donee, or (2) a judicial ruling by a judge. Until one of these occurs, the donee remains owner and can dispose of the object. According to Imam Zufar, revocation by mutual consent is a new contract, so the donee himself can later revoke, but the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that it is an annulment ab initio.

The passage includes hadith evidence: The hadith 'If the gift is to a mahram relative, he does not revoke it' (al-Hakim) and the athar of Ibn 'Umar. The Hanafi school uses these proofs to establish the ruling. The commentary also addresses the inter-madhhab dispute with Shafi'i who holds that the implication of the hadith (concept) gives a ruling for non-mahram, while Hanafis do not generally accept such implications but here rely on the athar.

Key Terms
الرجوع في الهبة (al-rujūʿ fī al-hibah): The right of the donor to rescind the gift and reclaim the gifted object after it has been given and possessed by the donee.
ذو رحم محرم (dhū raḥim muḥrim): A blood relative who is within the prohibited degrees of marriage, such as parents, children, siblings, uncles, aunts.
حكم الحاكم (ḥukm al-ḥākim): A judicial ruling by a judge to annul the gift, which is one of two valid methods of revocation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A man gives a gift to his cousin (ابن عم). Can he later revoke the gift according to the Hanafi school as explained in this passage?
A) Yes, because the cousin is not a mahram relative.
B) No, because all blood relatives prevent revocation.
C) Yes, because the cousin is a mahram relative.
D) No, because the gift was already given.

Key Takeaway
Revocation of gift is prevented in four specific cases: when the donee sells the gift, marries the donor, is a mahram relative, or when the gift is destroyed; revocation must be by mutual consent or judicial ruling.

Revocation of Gift for Mahram Relatives: Proof and Shafi'i Dispute
Ruling with proof and dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on revoking a gift to a mahram relative, identify the hadith proof, and explain why the Shafi'i school differs using the concept of mafhum al-mukhalafah.

Core Idea
A gift to a mahram relative is irrevocable; to a non-mahram, it is revocable unless compensated.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling that a gift to a mahram relative cannot be revoked. The ruling is based on a hadith authenticated by al-Hakim and an athar from Ibn 'Umar. Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees because he does not accept the implication (mafhum) of the hadith. We will explore the proof, the dispute, and some intra-Hanafi variations regarding slaves.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling that a gift to a mahram relative cannot be revoked. Note that 'mahram' includes blood and foster relatives within prohibited degrees.
The ruling is clear: revocation is haram for mahram donees.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i does not differentiate based on mahram; he holds that revocation may be permissible because he rejects mafhum al-mukhalafah as a valid legal source.
Shafi'i's position is rooted in usul al-fiqh methodology.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Shafi'i argues that the hadith only states a ruling for mahram; it does not logically imply the opposite for non-mahram. Thus, the hadith alone is insufficient to prohibit revocation for mahram.
Shafi'i requires explicit textual evidence for the opposite case.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school does not rely solely on mafhum; it also cites the explicit athar of Ibn 'Umar allowing revocation for non-mahram unless compensated. Additionally, the rationale is that the purpose of maintaining family ties is achieved for mahram.
The athar provides direct evidence for the non-mahram case.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafi prohibits revocation for mahram, Shafi'i may allow it under certain conditions. Also note intra-Hanafi differences when the donee is a slave of a relative.
This dispute has real-world implications for donors and donees.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الهبة ۱۳۵ الرجوع في الهبة لا يرجع فيها، والهاء الهلاك، فلو ادعاه صدق، وإنما يصح الرجوع . أي الواهب عن الهبة لا يرجع إلخ لحديث الحاكم مرفوعا : إذا كانت الهبة لذي رحم محرم لم يرجع فيها"، وصححه، وقال: على شرط الشيخين ومفهوم شرطه أنها إذا كانت لغير محرم فله الرجوع، فهو حجة على الشافعي له؛ لأنه قائل بلا رحم من : بالمفاهيم وأئمتنا وإن لم يعتبروه لكن صرح به في أثر ابن عمر لهما على ما رواه عبد الرزاق في "مصنفه" "من وهب هبة لغير ذي رحم، فله أن يرجع فيها إلا أن يثاب منها"، خرجه الحافظ الزيلعي، ولأنه قد حصل مقصوده، وهو صلة الرحم، أطلقه، فشمل المحرم المسلم والذمي والمستأمن كذا في "المبسوط". وقيد بالرحم؛ لأن المحرم كأخيه الرضاعة وأمهات النساء والربائب وأزواج البنين والبنات لا يمنع الرجوع. وقيد بالمحرم؛ لأن الرحم بلا محرم كابن عمه لا يمنع الرجوع، وفي ذكر القرابة ثم تفسيرها بالرحم المحرم إشارة إلى أنه لو وهب لرحم محرم لا من جهة القرابة كان له الرجوع كما لو وهب لابن عمه، وهو أخوه رضاعاً، وخرج ما لو وهب لعبد أخيه أو لأخيه وهو عبد لأجنبي، فإنه يرجع فيها عند أبي حنيفة؛ لأن الملك لم يقع فيها للقريب من كل وجه بدليل أن العبد أحق بما وهب إليه إذا احتاج إليه وقالا : لا يرجع في الأولى، ويرجع في الثانية، محرم من الواهب، فلا رجوع فيها اتفاقاً على الأصح؛ لأن الهبة لأيهما وقعت تمنع الرجوع رحم كذا في "المبسوط". [البحر الرائق: ٤٢٦/٧] والهاء الهلاك يعني هلاك العين الموهوبة مانع، وأما هلاك أحد العاقدين، فقد قدمه لتعذر الرجوع بعد الهلاك. [البحر الرائق: ٤٢٧/٧]
Book of Gift. Chapter on Revocation in Gift: He does not revoke in it. And the pronoun 'ha' refers to destruction. If he claims it, he is believed. And revocation is only valid... The meaning: The donor concerning the gift does not revoke, etc., due to the hadith of al-Hakim raised: 'When the gift is to a mahram relative, he does not revoke it.' And he authenticated it and said it is on the condition of the two shaykhs. And the implication of his condition is that if it is to a non-mahram, he may revoke it. So it is an argument against al-Shafi'i because he is a proponent of implications, and our imams did not consider them, but it is stated in the athar of Ibn 'Umar from them as recorded by 'Abd al-Razzaq in his Musannaf: 'Whoever gives a gift to a non-mahram relative, he may revoke it unless he receives compensation for it.' Extracted by al-Hafiz al-Zayla'i. And because his purpose, which is maintaining family ties, has been achieved. He made it absolute, so it includes mahram Muslim, dhimmi, and musta'min, as in al-Mabsut. And he restricted it to [mahram] relatives because non-mahram like a foster brother, mothers of women, step-daughters, and sons' wives and daughters do not prevent revocation. And he restricted it to mahram because a relative without mahram like a paternal cousin does not prevent revocation. And the mention of kinship then its interpretation as mahram relative indicates that if he gave to a mahram relative not through blood lineage, he may revoke, as if he gave to his paternal cousin while he is his foster brother. And excluded is if he gave to his brother's slave or to his brother while he is a slave of a foreigner, then Abu Hanifa says he revokes because ownership does not fully vest in the relative, evidenced by the slave's greater right to what is given to him if needed. And the two [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad] say: He does not revoke in the first, and revokes in the second. And if the donee is mahram to the donor, then there is no revocation by agreement according to the most correct view, because the gift to either of them prevents revocation. [Bahr al-Ra'iq: 7/426] And 'the pronoun ha refers to destruction' means destruction of the gifted item is a preventer. As for destruction of one of the contracting parties, it has been mentioned before that revocation becomes impossible after destruction. [Bahr al-Ra'iq: 7/427]
Source pages p. 136

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute ruling about revocation of gifts. The text begins by stating the ruling: a gift to a mahram relative cannot be revoked. The phrase 'the pronoun ha refers to destruction' is an explanation of the word 'ha' in the matn, indicating that destruction of the gifted item prevents revocation. Then the proof is given: the hadith from al-Hakim stating that a gift to a mahram relative cannot be revoked, and the converse implies that a gift to a non-mahram can be revoked. This is used as an argument against Imam al-Shafi'i, who does not consider implications (mafhum) as valid proof. However, our Hanafi imams do not rely on mafhum alone but also on the athar of Ibn 'Umar: a gift to a non-mahram can be revoked unless compensation is given. The ruling includes various conditions: mahram includes Muslim, dhimmi, and musta'min, but excludes foster brothers, etc. If the donee is a mahram relative even through fosterage, revocation is not allowed. The passage also discusses cases where the donee is a slave or a slave's relative, with a difference between Abu Hanifa and the two Sahibayn. The section ends by noting that destruction of the gifted item prevents revocation, as does the death of one of the contracting parties.

Key Terms
رحم محرم (rahim muharram): A blood relative within the prohibited degrees of marriage (mahram), such as parents, children, siblings, etc.
هبة (hibah): A gift; a contract that transfers ownership without compensation.
رجوع (ruju'): Revocation; the act of the donor taking back the gifted property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following gifts CANNOT be revoked?
A) A gift to a non-mahram relative who gave compensation
B) A gift to a mahram relative
C) A gift to a neighbor
D) A gift to a stranger

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prohibits revocation of gifts to mahram relatives, based on hadith and athar, and rejects the Shafi'i reliance on mafhum alone.

Donee's Claim of Destruction: Accepted Without Oath
Ruling statement that the donee's claim of destruction is accepted without oath, with contrast to lineage claim.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling that a donee's claim of destruction of the gifted property is accepted without oath and distinguish it from the case where the donee claims a lineage-based right.

Core Idea
A donee is believed without oath when claiming destruction because he denies the obligation to return.

In the law of gifts (hibah), a practical question arises if the donee says the gifted item was destroyed. Must he prove it or swear? The Hanafi school rules that the donee is believed without oath, as he is denying the obligation to return. This lesson unpacks the ruling and its limitation to claims of destruction only.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key ruling
The matn says 'If he claims it, he is believed.' Identify what 'it' refers to: destruction (halak). The donee's claim of destruction is accepted.
The pronoun 'hu' in 'ad'ahu' refers to destruction.
2
Understand the legal basis
The donee is believed because he is denying an obligation (al-inkar li wujub al-radd). In Hanafi procedural law, the defendant (denier) is generally believed without oath when denying an obligation.
This is a procedural principle: al-munkir yusaddaq bi yamin or without oath in certain contexts.
3
Note the restriction
The ruling is restricted to the claim of destruction. The text explicitly says 'qayyada bi da'wa al-hilak'. Other claims, like claiming brotherhood to prevent revocation, are treated differently.
The restriction prevents misuse of the rule.
4
Contrast with the brother claim case
If the donee claims to be the donor's brother (a mahram) and the donor denies, the donor is required to swear. This is because the claim involves establishing a necessary financial right due to lineage, so the purpose is to prove the financial right, not the lineage itself.
This distinction is cited from Qadi Khan's Fatawa.
5
Apply the principle
Practice: In a dispute, the donee says the gift has perished; the donor says it still exists. Who is believed? The donee, without oath. The donor may challenge, but the burden of proof is on him.
The donee's denial of liability is sufficient.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فلو ادعاه صدق: أي لو ادعى الموهوب له هلاك الموهوب يصدق؛ لأنه منكر لوجوب الرد عليه، قيد بدعوى الهلاك؛ لأن الموهوب له لو ادعى أنه أخوه وأنكره الواهب يستحلف الواهب عند الكل؛ لأنه ادعى بسبب النسب مالا لازما، فكان المقصود إثباته دون النسب، ذكره قاضي خان في "فتاواه" من "باب" الاستحلاف"، وأشار بقوله: "صدق" إلى أن القول قوله بغير يمين ولهذا قال في "الخلاصة": لو قال الموهوب له هلكت، فالقول قوله، ولا يمين عليه، فإن قال الواهب هي هذه حلف المنكر أنها ليست هذه إلخ. [البحر الرائق: ٤٢٧/٧]
'If he claims it, he is believed': i.e., if the donee claims destruction of the gifted item, he is believed because he is negating the obligation of returning it. It is restricted to the claim of destruction because if the donee claimed that he is the donor's brother and the donor denies it, the donor is made to take an oath according to all, because he claimed a necessary financial right due to lineage, so the purpose is to establish it rather than the lineage. Qadi Khan mentioned it in his Fatawa from the chapter on oath-taking. And he indicated by his statement 'he is believed' that his statement is accepted without oath, hence it is said in al-Khulasa: If the donee says 'It is destroyed', his statement is accepted and no oath is upon him. If the donor says 'It is this [i.e., still exists]', the denier [the donee] swears that it is not this, etc. [Bahr al-Ra'iq: 7/427]
Source pages p. 136

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement regarding the donee's claim of destruction of the gifted property. The matn says 'If he claims it, he is believed.' The commentary explains that the pronoun 'hu' refers to destruction. The donee is believed without oath because he is denying the obligation to return the property. This is contrasted with the case where the donee claims to be the donor's brother (a mahram relationship) to avoid revocation, in which case the donor is required to take an oath. The text clarifies that the donee's claim of destruction is accepted without the need for an oath, based on the principle that the party denying an obligation is believed.

Key Terms
قوله قوله (qawluhu qawluhu): His statement is accepted; meaning the person's claim is taken as true without requiring proof.
استحلاف (istihlaf): The act of requiring an oath from the other party in a dispute.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When a donee claims that the gifted item was destroyed, what is the ruling?
A) He must produce witnesses
B) He is believed without oath
C) He must return the item
D) The donor's statement is accepted

Key Takeaway
A donee's claim of destruction of a gifted item is accepted without oath because he is denying the obligation to return it.

Proper Method of Revoking a Gift: Mutual Consent or Judge's Decree
Ruling with intra-Hanafi dispute on revocation method

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two valid methods of revoking a gift according to the Hanafi school and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between the majority view and Imam Zufar regarding the legal nature of revocation by mutual consent.

Core Idea
Revocation of a gift is not unilateral; it requires mutual consent or a judge's decree, and is a rescission, not a new gift.

In Hanafi fiqh, a gift (hiba) becomes binding upon delivery, but the donor may revoke under specific conditions. This passage clarifies that revocation is only valid through mutual consent of both parties or by a judge's decree, and it functions as a rescission (faskh) of the original contract, not a new transaction. However, Imam Zufar, a prominent Hanafi scholar, dissents on the nature of mutual-consent revocation, leading to practical differences in the donee's rights. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its rationale, and the disputed nuance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
Read the passage to extract the two valid methods of revocation: mutual consent (taradi) of donor and donee, or a judge's decree (hukm al-hakim).
Any other form of revocation (e.g., unilateral action by the donor) is ineffective.
2
Understand the juristic rationale (ta'lil)
The text explains that once a contract is established and perfected, annulling it requires someone with authority to rescind – either the contracting parties (by mutual consent) or the judge (by decree). This is likened to returning a defective item after possession.
The analogy (qiyas) shows that revocation is a rescission, not a new contract.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute
Note that Imam Zufar (a Hanafi scholar) differs: he considers revocation by mutual consent to be a completely new gift contract (عقد جديد), not a rescission. This is the minority view within the school.
The majority view (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) treats it as a rescission.
4
Trace the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
If revocation is a rescission, the donee cannot revoke the revocation. If it is a new gift, the donee has the right to revoke that new gift as any donee would. Thus, Zufar gives the original donee a right to undo the revocation.
This affects the stability of the property transfer after revocation.
5
Determine the mufta bihi (operative ruling)
The majority view (rescission ab initio) is the relied-upon position for fatwa. Zufar's view is noted but not adopted in practice.
The text signals the preferred view by stating Zufar's opinion in contrast to the unmarked consensus.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإنما يصح الرجوع إلخ: أي وإنما يصح الرجوع عن الهبة بأحد الأمرين: إما بتراضيهما أي الواهب والموهوب له، أو بحكم الحاكم بالرجوع؛ لأن حكم العقد قد ثبت وتم والرفع بعد الثبوت يتوقف على فسخ من له ولاية الفسخ، وهو القاضي والمتعاقدان كالرد بالعيب بعد القبض، فما لم يقض القاضي أو لم يفسخاها بالتراضي، فملك الموهوب له ثابت في العين حتى ينفذ تصرفه فيه من عتق وبيع وغير ذلك ولو كان بعد المرافعة إلى الحاكم، وكذا لو منعه، وهلك في يده لا يضمن؛ لقيام ملكه فيه وكذا لو هلك بعد القضاء قبل المنع، وإن منعه بعد القضاء ضمن؛ لوجود التعدي، وبكل منهما أي بالرضاء وبالقضاء يكون فسخا من الأصل، وعند زفر الله: الرجوع بالتراضي عقد جديد، فجعل بمنزلة الهبة المبتدأة، فكان للموهوب له الرجوع. [رمز الحقائق: ٢٦٥/٢]
'And revocation is only valid, etc.': i.e., revocation of a gift is valid only by one of two things: either by mutual consent of the donor and donee, or by the judge's decree of revocation. Because the effect of the contract has been established and completed, and annulling it after establishment depends on a rescission by one who has the authority to rescind, and that is the judge or the two contracting parties, like the return due to a defect after possession. So as long as the judge has not decreed or they have not rescinded it by mutual consent, the donee's ownership remains in the item such that his disposition (like freeing a slave, selling, etc.) is effective, even after litigation to the judge. Similarly, if the donor prevents him [from using] and the item is destroyed in his hand, he does not guarantee because his ownership is intact. Likewise, if it is destroyed after the decree but before prevention, he does not guarantee. But if he prevents him after the decree, he guarantees because of transgression. And by each of these (mutual consent or decree), it is a rescission ab initio. According to Zufar (may Allah have mercy on him), revocation by mutual consent is a new contract, so it is treated like an initial gift, and thus the donee has the right to revoke. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 2/265]
Source pages p. 136

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute ruling about the method of revoking a gift. The text states that revocation is valid only by mutual consent of both parties or by a judge's decree. The reason is that the contract is fully established, and annulling it requires the authority of those who can rescind, namely the contracting parties or the judge. As long as neither has rescinded, the donee's ownership is fully effective, so his actions (like selling or freeing a slave) are valid. If the donor prevents the donee after the judge's decree, the donor becomes liable. There is a dispute with Zufar, who holds that revocation by mutual consent is a completely new contract, like a new gift, so the donee retains the right to revoke again. This difference affects the rights of the parties.

Key Terms
تراضيهما (taradihi ma): Mutual consent of both the donor and the donee to revoke the gift.
فسخ (faskh): Rescission; annulment of a contract ab initio.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what happens if the donor tries to unilaterally revoke a gift without mutual consent or a judge's decree?
A) The donee's ownership is unaffected
B) The gift is automatically revoked
C) The donor must pay compensation
D) The donee must return the item

Key Takeaway
Revocation of a gift is valid only by mutual consent of both parties or by a judge's decree; the Hanafi school treats it as a rescission ab initio, not a new gift.

Donee's Lack of Recourse Against Donor When Gift is Destroyed and Reclaimed
Ruling on donee's lack of recourse after third-party claim on gift

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling that a donee has no recourse against the donor when a gifted item is destroyed and a third party recovers it, and explain the legal reasoning based on the nature of gratuitous contracts.

Core Idea
In a gift, the donee bears the risk; the donor is not liable because a gift is a gratuitous contract.

This lesson examines a specific scenario in the law of gifts (hibah): what happens when the gifted property is destroyed and then a rightful owner appears and recovers damages from the donee? The passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq and its commentary from al-Fath clarify that the donee cannot seek compensation from the donor. The reason lies in the classification of a gift as a gratuitous contract, which imposes no warranty of safety on the donor.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Read the passage and state the explicit ruling: the donee does not have recourse against the donor for the amount he paid to the rightful claimant.
2
Locate the legal cause (illah)
The passage explains that the ruling is because a gift is a 'aqd tabarru' (gratuitous contract), so the attribute of safety is not required. This means the donor does not guarantee the item's safety for the donee.
The term 'tabarru' is key - it indicates a voluntary transfer without compensation.
3
Understand the contrast
The commentary contrasts the gift with deposit (wadi'ah) and lease (ijarah). In those contracts, the contract is for the benefit of the depositor/lessor, so the depositor/lessor bears the risk. In a gift, possession is for the donee's benefit, so he bears the risk.
This contrast highlights the importance of identifying who the contract primarily benefits.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن تلفت الموهوبة إلخ : أي وإن تلفت العين الموهوبة واستحقها مستحق، وضمن المستحق الموهوب له، لم يرجع على الواهب بما ضمن. (مسكين) قال في "الفتح": قوله: "لم يرجع على الواهب"؛ لأنها عقد تبرع، فلا يستحق فيه وصف السلامة والإعارة كالهبة؛ لأن قبض المستعير كان لنفسه، بخلاف الوديعة والعين المستأجرة؛ لأن العقد فيهما يكون للدافع. (فتح)
'If the gifted item is destroyed, etc.': i.e., if the gifted item is destroyed and it is claimed by a rightful claimant, and the claimant causes the donee to pay [damages], the donee does not have recourse against the donor for what he paid. (Miskin) Al-Fath says: 'He does not have recourse against the donor' because it is a gratuitous contract, so the attribute of safety is not required in it, like aariyah (loan for use); for the borrower's possession is for himself, unlike a deposit or a leased item, because the contract in those cases is for the benefit of the depositor/lessor. (Fath)
Source pages p. 137

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the donee's position when the gifted item is destroyed and a third party establishes ownership and recovers damages from the donee. The ruling is that the donee cannot claim compensation from the donor. The proof is that a gift is a gratuitous contract (tabarru'), so the donor does not guarantee the item's safety for the donee, similar to a loan (aariyah). In contrast, in a contract of deposit (wadi'ah) or lease (ijarah), the contract is for the benefit of the depositor/lessor, so the bailee/lessee can claim if the item is reclaimed. Since the donee's possession is for his own benefit, he bears the risk.

Key Terms
عقد تبرع (aqd tabarru'): A gratuitous contract where one party gives without receiving compensation.
إعارة (i'anah): Loan for use; a contract where one allows another to use an item without compensation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a gifted item is destroyed and a third party rightfully claims ownership from the donee, what is the donee's right?
A) He can claim the value from the donor
B) He has no recourse against the donor
C) He can return the item to the donor
D) He can demand compensation from the third party

Key Takeaway
A donee has no recourse against the donor for compensation paid to a third party who rightfully reclaims the gifted item, because a gift is a gratuitous contract where the donee bears the risk.

Hibah bi Shart al-'Iwad: Gift Initially, Sale Ultimately
Definition and ruling on hibah bi shart al-'iwad.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on hibah bi shart al-'iwad, explain its dual nature, and apply the conditions for its validity.

Core Idea
Hibah bi shart al-'iwad is a gift initially and a sale ultimately, marrying gift and sale rules.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq explains the unique hybrid contract of a gift given with a condition of compensation. The Hanafi school treats it as a gift initially, requiring delivery in the session and prohibiting undivided shares, but after compensation, it becomes a sale with all its consequences, including defect return and pre-emption. Understanding this distinction is crucial for identifying the correct rulings in such transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its category
Hibah bi shart al-'iwad is a hybrid: it has elements of both gift and sale. Initially, it is a gift; after compensation, it becomes a sale.
2
Apply the rules of gift initially
As a gift, conditions include exchange of possession in the session and prohibition of undivided shares (shuyu') if the item can be partitioned.
3
Transition to sale after compensation
After both parties take possession, the transaction becomes a sale. Sale rules apply: return for defect, option of inspection, and pre-emption (shuf'ah) if real estate.
4
Note the dispute with Zufar and al-Shafi'i
Zufar (within Hanafi) and al-Shafi'i consider it a pure sale from the start. Their evidence: it is an exchange of property for property.
5
Identify the practical difference
The thamarah al-khilaf: according to them, sale-related rights exist before delivery; according to Hanafi, only after delivery.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الهبة بشرط العوض هبة ابتداء بيع انتهاء، فيشترط التقابض في العوضين وتبطل بالشيوع بيع انتهاء، فيرد بالعيب وخيار الرؤية، وتؤخذ بالشفعة. أي إن كان عقارا. هبة ابتداء إلخ: اعلم أن الهبة بشرط العوض يشتمل على جهتين من جهة هبة ومن جهة بيع، فيجمع بينهما ما أمكن عملا بالشبهين، وقد أمكن؛ لأن الهبة من حكمها تأخر الملك إلى القبض، وقد يتراخى عن البيع الفاسد، والبيع حكمه اللزوم، وقد تنقلب الهبة لازمة بالتعويض، فجمعنا بينهما، وقلنا: إنها هبة ابتداء وبيع انتهاء، وإذا كانت هبة ابتداء، فيشترط فيها ما يشترط في الهبة من التقابض في المجلس مطلقا، سواء كان بإذنه أو بلا إذنه، وبعده بإذنه؛ لأن القبض شرط في الهبة كما مر وكل واحد منهما واهب من وجه ويبطلها الشيوع فيما يحتمل القسمة كما يبطل الهبة بلا شرط العوض؛ لأن هبة المشاع لا تصح كما مر ، وصورة الهبة بشرط العوض أن يقول: وهبتك هذا الشيء على أن تعوضني كذا، وأما إذا قال بالباء بأن قال: وهبتك هذا العبد بثوبك هذا أو بألف درهم، فهو بيع وانتهاء، هذا حاصل ما في الشروح مع توضيح. بيع انتهاء إلخ : أي الهبة بشرط العوض بيع انتهاء يعني بعد القبض، حتى لو تقابضا . العقد، صح وصار في حكم البيع، وإذا كانت بيعا انتهاء فيرد الموهوب بالعيب وخيار الرؤية لأحدهما، ويؤخذ بالشفعة إذا كان أحد العوضين عقارا، وهذا عندنا، وعند زفر والشافعي: بيع ابتداء وانتهاء؛ لأنها تمليك ببدل من الابتداء، فكان بيعا، ولنا: أن الموجود قبل القبض ليس إلا الهبة المشروط بالعوض، وإنما نأخذ حكم مبادلة المال بالمال بعد التعويض، فكان هبة ابتداء وبيعا انتهاء، وثمرة الخلاف: أن عندهم يثبت خيار الرؤية والرد بالعيب قبل القبض، ويجوز في مشاع يحتمل القسمة، وعندنا : لا يثبت شيء من الأحكام قبل القبض. من العيني وغيره بتوضيح من المحشي)
Gift with the condition of compensation is a gift initially and a sale ultimately. So delivery of both compensations is required, and it is invalidated by undivided share (shuyu'), and ultimately it is a sale, so it is returned due to defect and option of inspection, and it is subject to pre-emption if the gifted item is real estate. 'Hibah initially, etc.': Know that hibah with compensation has two aspects: a gift aspect and a sale aspect. So we combine both as much as possible by applying both similarities. This is possible because the ruling of gift is that ownership is delayed until delivery, and it may be delayed from a defective sale, and the ruling of sale is bindingness, and gift becomes binding with compensation. So we combined them and said: It is a gift initially and a sale ultimately. And when it is a gift initially, the conditions of gift apply, such as exchange of possession in the session absolutely, whether with or without his permission, and after it with his permission, because possession is a condition in gift. And each of them is a donor in one sense. And it is invalidated by undivided share in something that can be partitioned, just as a gift without compensation is invalidated because a gift of undivided share is not valid. The form of hibah with compensation is when one says: 'I gift you this thing on condition that you compensate me with such-and-such.' But if he says with the preposition 'bi': 'I gift you this slave for your cloth or for a thousand dirhams,' then it is a sale entirely. This is the summary from the commentaries with clarification. 'Sale ultimately, etc.': i.e., hibah with compensation is a sale ultimately after possession, so if they exchange possession in the contract, it is valid and becomes like a sale. And when it is a sale ultimately, the gifted item is returnable due to defect and option of inspection for either party, and it is subject to pre-emption if one of the compensations is real estate. This is our position. According to Zufar and al-Shafi'i: it is a sale entirely from beginning to end, because it is transferring ownership in exchange for a consideration from the start. Our proof is that what exists before possession is only the gift conditioned on compensation, and we only apply the rules of exchange after compensation, so it is a gift initially and a sale ultimately. The practical difference is that according to them, the options of inspection and return due to defect exist before possession, and it is permissible in an undivided share that can be partitioned. According to us, none of these rulings are established before possession. (From al-'Ayni and others with clarification from the marginal annotator)
Source pages p. 137

Commentary
This passage is a definition ruling on hibah bi shart al-'iwad (gift with condition of compensation). The text defines it as a gift initially and a sale ultimately. This hybrid nature is necessary to honor both aspects. Initially, the rules of gift apply: delivery is required in the session, and it is invalid if the item is undivided. After compensation, the rules of sale apply: the item can be returned due to defects, there is an option of inspection, and pre-emption applies if it is real estate. The text distinguishes this from a transaction phrased with the preposition 'bi', which is a pure sale. There is a dispute with Zufar and al-Shafi'i, who consider it a pure sale from the start. The practical difference is that in their view, the sale rules apply before delivery, while in the Hanafi view, they only apply after delivery.

Key Terms
هبة بشرط العوض (hibah bi shart al-'iwad): A gift given on the condition that the donee compensates the donor with something specific.
التقابض في المجلس (at-taqabud fi al-majlis): Mutual exchange of possession in the same sitting, a condition for the validity of hibah.
الشيوع (ash-shuyu'): Undivided share; an item that is owned in common with others and not partitioned.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when does the right of pre-emption (shuf'ah) apply in hibah bi shart al-'iwad?
A) Immediately upon the contract
B) Only after delivery and compensation
C) Only if the donor is a mahram
D) It never applies

Key Takeaway
Hibah bi shart al-'iwad is a hybrid: initial gift rules (possession, no shuyu') apply before compensation, and sale rules (defect return, pre-emption) apply after compensation.
